Our Army Cannot Retreat from Longmensuo 30

Increased Troops There is Unconfirmed

A Formal Reply has been Given to the Japanese Side

Song Zheyuan Arrived in Beiping Last Night

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan arrived in Beiping at 11:50 PM on the 22nd. He stated that the Japanese Eighth Division's claim of our increasing troops and artillery at Longmensuo has been formally denied on the evening of the 22nd. Our army at Longmensuo is located within our own territory, and its mission is to suppress bandits, so it cannot retreat. He will return to Chahar after attending the Standing Committee meeting of the Military Affairs Commission on the 24th. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Shibayama recently received a telegram from Nishi Yoshiichi stating that the 29th Army in Chahar Province had increased its infantry by 1,000 men and artillery by 60 pieces along the Great Wall line and should quickly withdraw within the Great Wall; otherwise, decisive measures would be taken. After receiving the telegram, Shibayama went to Jurentang to visit He Yingqin and requested that he quickly order the increased garrison along the Great Wall to withdraw. He then summoned Qin Dechun for consultation. Qin stated that the Chahar provincial authorities had never transferred troops to the Great Wall line and requested that He refute the claim. He and Huang, considering that there were many future problems in eastern Chahar, telegraphed Song Zheyuan to come to Beiping for consultation with the Japanese representative. Song is planning to come to Beiping tonight or tomorrow morning. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Liu Shisun went to Tianjin this afternoon to visit Song. He said that regarding the Chahar East incident, he was assigned to negotiate with the Japanese Embassy's military attaché, Nemoto. The Japanese army has already withdrawn. Currently, an agreement has been made with the Japanese side to negotiate in Beiping. Huang specially summoned Song back to Beiping to find a proper solution to the Chahar East situation. The Japanese representative has not yet been appointed. Song will return to Chahar after the negotiations have reached a certain stage. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan arrived in Beiping from Tianjin at 11:40 PM on the 22nd and is scheduled to visit He and Huang on the morning of the 23rd to discuss important matters. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Song Zheyuan came to Tianjin to visit his mother. Recently, due to the tense situation in eastern Chahar, he returned to Beiping to defend. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) Fu Chun's troops have been reorganized into a regiment and placed under the control of Zhang Zizhong's division. The Chicheng, Dushikou, Longmensuo, and Zhaojiaying areas in eastern Chahar are still garrisoned by Zhang Renjie and Zhang Yunrong's troops, with no increase in troops. The Japanese side's excuse is obviously pre-meditated. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Diplomatic sources say that the Chahar East incident has been completely resolved through negotiations between the Ping Political Affairs Commission, the Military Affairs Commission, and the Japanese side. The Japanese and puppet troops who attacked Longmensuo have now withdrawn. However, the military and political authorities in North China believe that the Japanese army is deliberately misinterpreting the Tanggu Truce Agreement and is using bandit suppression as a pretext to encroach upon us. If this continues, the future is worrisome. It is reported that the central government has been informed in detail and has been asked to provide a post-settlement policy and that the plenary session should conduct a thorough discussion of the diplomatic problems of North China and provide guidance for compliance. (22nd Special Dispatch)

Mongolian Representatives Meet Chairman Lin 31

Requesting Adoption of the Original Autonomy Outline

Declaring that They Cannot Accept the Measures Determined by the Political Council

(Nanjing) More than ten representatives from the Mongolian leagues visited Chairman Lin of the National Government on the morning of the 22nd, introduced by Shi Qingyang. Chairman Lin extended his encouragement to the representatives and inquired about the current situation in Inner Mongolia in great detail. The representatives expressed the desire of Inner Mongolia for autonomy and requested the adoption of the original autonomy outline. Lin replied that if it did not conflict with the principles of autonomy determined by the central government, it could be adopted. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Representatives from Mongolia requesting autonomy in Nanjing issued a statement, which read: "Regarding the solemn declaration, the representatives learned on the afternoon of January 16 of the results of the Central Political Council's Legislative Group's re-examination of the Mongolian autonomy case. The eleven articles agreed upon by Minister Huang in Bailingmiao were completely changed. Alarmed, we could not sleep all night. January 17 was the date of the Central Political Council meeting. At 7:00 AM, we met with representatives of various leagues and banners stationed in Nanjing and presented a document to the Central Political Council requesting the maintenance of the original plan agreed upon in Bailingmiao. We also presented the photocopied petition to each member of the council as they arrived, requesting their support. When the Central Political Council sent Secretary-General Tang to meet us, we verbally explained the situation in detail, urging the maintenance of the original plan and, at the very least, requesting that room be left for maneuver. We were promised that it would be relayed, and we were strongly urged to return first. At noon, we returned to our residence to await orders. Unexpectedly, the Central Political Council still made a decision based on the results of the review that day. The decision was published in the newspapers on the 18th. After carefully reading it several times, we were shocked. The Central Political Council's decision also consisted of eleven articles, but they were completely opposite to the eleven articles agreed upon in Bailingmiao. The representatives were sent to Nanjing to request the early implementation of the original plan agreed upon in Bailingmiao and to thank the central government for its good intentions. Now that the Central Political Council's decision is completely contrary to the original plan, the representatives absolutely dare not accept it. In addition to separately listing the parts of the Central Political Council's decision that are not suitable for the Mongolian people and reporting the above situation to the government while informing officials and civilians of each league and banner, we hereby solemnly declare that we absolutely cannot accept the eleven articles of the Mongolian autonomy plan decided by the Central Political Council on January 17. We hope that our compatriots will grant us their understanding." (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) He Yaozu hosted a banquet for the Mongolian representatives at the Lishi Society on the 22nd. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

In the past, the symbol of German unity was the imperial crown; today, it is the swastika. Germans look to the future, feeling that the symbols of the imperial crown and the swastika embody the same ideology, namely that the duty of the German people is to fulfill their mission to the world and Western culture. This great national unity has united the German states, provinces, counties, towns, villages, all occupations, all ages, and all classes of society, rich and poor, wise and foolish, into one body. The breadth of its scope and the firmness of its unity are unprecedented. The German people are not troubled by the difficulties of their current position. Germany does not want to pursue imperialist policies, nor does it want to attack anyone, but insists on having a corresponding position among sovereign nations. This is not the kind of ideology that Daladier referred to in the Senate on January 18 as inciting various national sentiments, but merely the ideology of a great nation having the right to a glorious existence. Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs Declares No Intention to Wage War Against Russia 57

Says Not a Single Soldier Has Been Sent to the Border

(Tokyo) Recently, there have been widespread rumors in the Soviet Union about the crisis of war between Japan and Russia, and figures such as the French political heavyweight Herriot have continued to spread rumors about the cloud of war in the Far East. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs specifically issued a statement on the 22nd to refute these rumors. At the same time, it clarified the fundamental policy of Japanese diplomacy, saying that Soviet government officials, People's Commissar Council Chairman Molotov, Foreign Affairs People's Commissar Litvinov, Red Army Military Revolutionary Committee General Budyonny, etc., have been giving speeches at the Central Executive Committee since last year, pointing out that Japan is preparing for war and stating that Japan is plotting to seize the Chinese Eastern Railway. On the other hand, public speeches by former French Prime Minister Herriot and US Ambassador to Russia Bullitt also stated that war between Japan and Russia was imminent. The Japanese government has maintained a calm attitude towards the Soviet Union's repeated challenging attitude. In the past, when the Soviet Union issued documents, it also used a calm attitude to correct its reflections. It has always sought to resolve various pending issues between Japan and Russia by peaceful means. That is, in the negotiations for the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, Japan actively mediated. When the Soviet Union某结 stationed troops on the Russian-Manchurian border, Japan, because it was responsible for joint defense under the Japan-Manchukuo Treaty, did not send a single soldier to the border area. The Japanese government's attitude is so determined, but the Soviet Union has recently continued to make challenging remarks. Japan finds it difficult to understand the reasons for this. If the Soviet Union continues this attitude, the result will not only create an atmosphere of unease between the two countries, but also cause third-country aircraft to be used to create a crisis between Japan and Russia. (22nd Japan Federation News Agency Telegram)

Herriot Discusses the Crisis in the Far East, France is Unwilling to Intervene 59

Tensions Between the US, Russia, and Japan Intensify

Only Willing to Offer Well-Intentioned Mediation

(Paris) Former Prime Minister and current Chairman of the House of Representatives Foreign Affairs Committee Herriot has recently written an article entitled "The Tripartite Balance of Power," which will be published by the Economic and Financial News Agency on Sunday. The so-called "Tripartite Balance of Power" in the article refers to the three major powers of Russia, the United States, and Japan. The conflict between these three major powers is gradually becoming tense, which is a cause of concern for the world. Herriot first mentions the important speech on the Far East issue recently given by Soviet Foreign Affairs Commissar Litvinov at the Fourth Plenary Session of the Soviet Central Executive Committee. Herriot analyzes the key to the Far East issue based on this declaration by Litvinov.

Disputes over the Chinese Eastern Railway 60

He roughly states that since Japan waged war in Manchuria and created "Manchukuo," the Soviet Union has become alarmed about its interests in the Chinese Eastern Railway. The Soviet Union then held preliminary negotiations with Japan on purchasing the Chinese Eastern Railway. According to Soviet observations, Japan is engaging in military preparations on the Manchurian border. Therefore, the Russian government has no choice but to set up fortifications and increase defenses on the border. Herriot believes that whether or not the negotiations for the purchase of the Chinese Eastern Railway can be successfully concluded is the key to peace and war. Herriot continues to analyze Litvinov's speech, saying that Litvinov declared in the conclusion that the Soviet Union is determined not to allow an inch of territory to be ceded to others. Therefore, the Soviet Union will continue to increase its land, sea, and air military equipment. Later, during a period of repeated disputes, the Soviet Union reconciled with the United States, and the United States and Russia resumed diplomatic relations, and the situation in the Far East changed again. However, the management of the Chinese Eastern Railway still caused frequent troubles. Both Russia and Japan

Both parties are greatly disturbed and uneasy. Whenever a dispute arises, both parties seize the opportunity to use it as an excuse to attack each other.

Naval Competition Between the US and Japan 61

(Omitted)... On the Japanese side, they are also paying close attention to the policies of the United States, especially the naval armaments of the United States. From this point of view, there is no doubt that the situation between Japan and the United States, and between Japan and the Soviet Union, is tense. This situation cannot be said to be without danger. Japan needs territory to accommodate its surplus population and needs markets to sell its exports. Japan's needs make some major powers regard it as a hidden concern. At the same time, some parties in Japan are loudly advocating militarism. All of these factors have created a difficult situation. In addition, the naval issue between Japan and the United States and the Chinese Eastern Railway issue between Japan and Russia have made the widespread and long-standing Far East issue even more acute.

British Navy Conference in Singapore, British Generals to Decide on Policy Towards Japan 62

MacDonald Cabinet Members Vacillate

Mostly Inclined to Contact the United States

(Washington) According to Washington's observers studying the situation in the Far East, British policy toward Japan may have a major decision at the British Empire Naval Conference that opens on Thursday in Singapore. Although London officials are unwilling to express the significance of this conference, informed sources here recognize this as the first Imperial naval gathering in the Far East in five years, and attach special importance to it at the same time as the new global naval competition. Although the British government, due to economic relations, has decided not to proceed with the construction of the Singapore naval base, reliable sources in London reveal that the naval base will still need to be completed by the end of 1938 or early 1939. This can be seen as an expression of unease from London, Australia, and New Zealand about Japan's ambitions. However, according to other sources, the British government still wants to improve British-Japanese relations, believing that this is the only key to guaranteeing peace in the Pacific. It is said that naval experts in London even believe that the fighting strength of the Japanese Navy is stronger than that of the US Navy. It is said that most members of the MacDonald Cabinet are inclined towards the United States on the Far East issue, but on the one hand, they are still unwilling to offend Japan. The British naval generals attending the Singapore Conference are the Commander-in-Chief of the China Fleet, the Commander-in-Chief of the East Indies Fleet, and key personnel from Australia and New Zealand. The Naval Situation of the Powers (1) 66

(Foreign Affairs Review Agency) The New Year's special edition of the Japanese magazine "Diplomatic Times" states:

1. The Relationship Between Land, Sea, and Air Forces

Generally, those who observe the future need to thoroughly study the past and the present. Mahan, based on historical research, derived various lessons for the future. Colonel Maas, the current Director of War Plans for the US Navy, stated, "The prediction of the future should be based on past actions and current situations. In dealing with future matters, our guiding principle is nothing more than the measures that constitute the basis for prediction."

Therefore, to understand the future naval situation of the powers, we must start by examining the past situation.

Armaments exist to support the implementation of national policy. Conflicts of national policy will inevitably lead to the opposition of armaments. If armaments include land and sea forces, countries with deeper connections to the land will prioritize the army, while countries with deeper connections to the ocean will prioritize the navy. However, all major countries in the world are related to the ocean to varying degrees, and none can afford not to maintain naval power. The main ones are the five countries of Britain, the United States, France, Italy, and Japan.

The ocean connects all countries, and therefore, the navy that floats on the sea also has a universal character. The above five countries all have naval interests, and those countries that are directly adjacent have particularly deep relationships. For example, although land power occupies an important position in France and Germany, which are neighboring countries, naval power is also quite important. Furthermore, the naval relationship between Japan and the United States is even more important. In short, the five major naval powers are not only opposed to each other in the world but also confront other smaller naval powers locally.

Recently, due to the development of aircraft, the division between land and sea forces has undergone tremendous changes. On November 3 of last year, the British Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs stated, "As a result of the development of the air force, Britain cannot act as an island and adopt an isolationist policy." Purely maritime countries originally relied on the navy to ensure national defense, but now, as a result of the development of aircraft, they are also afraid of the threat posed by the air power of other countries. Therefore, those who discuss the navy must also discuss the air force.

Will the Washington and London Treaties, which Japan is dissatisfied with, be revised, remain effective, or be abandoned in 1935? A naval disarmament conference will be held to discuss this issue. The outcome of the conference will have a significant impact on the world's naval situation. Therefore, it is necessary to examine the issue of disarmament.

The purpose of this article is to explore the naval situation of the powers after 1936 and to deduce their mutual relations and the lessons for Japan's national defense based on the national policies and naval power of the five major naval powers. (To be continued)

Situation of the Panchen Lama's Arrival in Beiping 85

The Panchen Lama Will Arrive in Beijing to Discuss Tibetan Affairs

Ma Bufang Welcomes the Panchen Lama's Return to Tibet

Beiping Correspondence: Panchen Erdeni, the Great Master of Protecting the Nation and Spreading Enlightenment, recently left Bailing Temple for Suiyuan. On the morning of the 18th, at 10:00 AM, he transferred from Suiyuan to a specially prepared train southward. The train was extremely beautiful. The locomotive was numbered 117. The Panchen Lama's own flower car was numbered 101. The sleeper car for the Khenpos and secretaries was numbered 231. The dining car was numbered 170. These were all requisitioned from the Beining Railway. The remaining cars consisted of first-class car 251, third-class cars 110 and 112, two flat cars for luggage, and four open cars for transporting 15 automobiles. These were all cars from the Pingsui Railway. The train arrived in Zhangjiakou at 6:00 AM today (the 19th) and departed at 7:00 AM. The journey was slower due to strong north winds. Accompanying him were Senji Khenpo, Da Zhuoni Khenpo, Dafu Khenpo, Zhao Zhuoni Khenpo, Secretary-General Liu Jiaju, Secretaries Li Yufeng and Xie Yongzhao, ten guards, ten sutra-chanting lamas, and 68 staff members in total. Central Government representative Leng Rong, Suiyuan Provincial Government Deputy Adjutant Yao, Director of the Panchen Lama's Suiyuan Office Ding Wang Duo Ji, and Deputy Director of the Beijing Office Zhu Haishan also traveled with the train. Upon arrival in Beiping at 5:00 PM, groups welcoming the Panchen Lama at the station included the Beiping Hengshan General Society, the Shanhua Buddhist Association, the Puji Buddhist Association, the Yonghe Temple, the Fuxiang Temple, the Puyou Temple, lamas, monks, nuns, the Puming Buddhist Association, the Lay Buddhist Forest, the Lotus Sect Pure Land Society Nianfo Society, the Women's Buddhist Studies Association, the Yonglan Buddhist Women's Association, the Buddhist Association, the Zixia Jixuan Xuan, the Mongolian-Tibetan Fellow-Villagers Association, the Beijing Office of the Mongolian-Tibetan Affairs Commission, the Mongolian-Tibetan School, and the Qingkang Beiping Students Association. Mongol princes present included Nayantu, Ubaudutubobo, Amurkingelatu, Tong Haifeng, Ningxia Provincial Government Committee Member Dali Zazhaya, Zhangjia representative Li Shoushan, Gong Shushi. Representatives from the military and political circles included He Yingqin's representative Xu Ying, Yuan Liang's representative Liu Yuhu, Director of the Public Security Bureau Yu Jin Su, representative of the British Embassy Taikeman, Counselor Harada of the Japanese Embassy, and Chinese and foreign Buddhist disciples Wang Wenjin, Wang Wenyu, Tan Shuyuan, Yang YiWu, Song Ying, Gu Chongxin, Xue Jimin, Ye Zhongji, Lu Fengsheng, Guo Changhe, Geng Ruitian, Xiao Shufang, Liu Biqiu, Dai Chuanxian, Dean of the Examination Yuan, Lin Xiang. After the special train passed through Xizhimen, the Beijing East Railway Station was tightly guarded by a platoon of station gendarmes, the Fourth Team of the Public Security Bureau's security forces, and special agents. When the Panchen Lama alighted from the train, many Buddhist men and women raised a piece of yellow silk they had prepared, which the Panchen Lama placed on their heads as a blessing. After leaving the station, the Panchen Lama boarded a specially prepared car and drove to the Fengze Garden residence in Zhongnanhai.

According to a statement released by the Panchen Lama, he said that he had repeatedly received telegrams from important figures of the Central Government urging him to come to Beijing to discuss Mongolian and Tibetan border affairs. Therefore, he did not plan to stay in Beiping for long. However, due to a cough and headache, the date of his journey to Beijing was still uncertain. He had not yet decided whether he would be able to attend the Fourth Plenary Session. Therefore, he had not prepared any proposals. If the opportunity arose, he would report on the actual situation in Mongolia and Tibet. Regarding the issue of returning to Tibet, he had been in constant sorrow since the passing of the Dalai Lama. He had not considered how to manage Tibetan affairs. However, the matter of returning to Tibet would have to be decided after consultations with the Central Government. He planned to stay in Beijing for two months. According to a statement by the Panchen Lama's Secretary-General Liu Jiaju, the Panchen Lama had been away from Tibet for twelve years and had always been thinking of returning. The Dalai Lama and the Panchen Lama had a harmonious personal relationship. After the passing of the Dalai Lama, the Panchen Lama did not eat for a week. In addition to discussing the issue of returning to Tibet with the Central Government, the Panchen Lama's visit to Beijing also had the important tasks of commemorating the Dalai Lama and coordinating the issue of Inner Mongolian autonomy. There was no question that the Panchen Lama would return to Tibet. When he returns north in the future, he may first go to Qinghai. The Qinghai Propaganda Office had already been established in Xiangde. More than 150 pieces of luggage and a radio station had been transported there. The rumor that Ma Bufang held objections was completely inaccurate. Because he and the director of the Beijing Office, Luo Sang Jianzan, had met with Ma Bufang in Nanjing last September, and Ma had expressed a warm welcome. Furthermore, the people of Qinghai and various quarters in Tibet had sent a flood of telegrams welcoming the Panchen Lama's return to Tibet, which proved that his words were not false. Deputy Director of the Beijing Office Zhu Haishan had previously been ordered to go to Qinghai. Because the results of the consultations were satisfactory, he recently flew from Beiping to Suiyuan to visit the Panchen Lama and report everything. This also proved that the rumors were not credible. (19th)

He Yingqin Sends Personnel to Visit Yan Xishan to Jointly Discuss the Mediation of Sun Ma 86

Hou Cheng Arrives in Taiyuan with a Mission

Requesting Yan Xishan to Eliminate the Scourge of War

Taiyuan Correspondence: Since the conflict between the Sun and Ma armies in western Suiyuan, the situation in the Northwest has suddenly become tense. As Sun Dianying and Yan Xishan have long been comrades in arms, and Yan and Sun have a close relationship forged in adversity, it is most appropriate and effective for Yan to mediate the matter or directly order Sun to cease military actions. Therefore, since the incident occurred, the Central Government, Chairman Chiang, Minister He, and others have telegraphed Yan, requesting him to quickly dissuade Sun to avoid escalating the situation. Ma Hongkui also sent a representative to Taiyuan to visit Yan and report on the situation. The Beiping Military Council believes that Sun's actions are of great importance to the Northwest frontier defense and should be resolved quickly. In addition to numerous consultations with Yan by telegram in recent days, the Beiping Military Council has specially sent Hou Cheng, a councilor of the Beiping Military Council, to Taiyuan this afternoon (the 18th) to visit Yan with a personal letter from He Yingqin, presenting everything in person. Hou stayed at the Shanxi Hotel. Both the Suiyuan and Shanxi authorities sent personnel to receive him. According to Hou's statement, "After receiving reports of the conflict between the Sun and Ma armies in Ningbian, Chairman He immediately telegraphed both sides, urging them to first cease military actions and send personnel to investigate the truth. Now, because Director Yan has a deep friendship with Commander Sun, in addition to the Central Government's telegram to Yan requesting him to find a way to eliminate the conflict, he was sent to Taiyuan to present everything in person, requesting immediate and vigorous mediation to resolve the dispute. Tonight or tomorrow morning, he will visit the Suiyuan authorities to visit Yan. Regarding Sun Dianying's troops, the Beiping Military Council stipulated that when allocating funds to the various armies in North China, this army was allocated a monthly subsidy of 200,000 yuan from the Military Council. In addition to six infantry regiments, special service and cavalry units of about two regiments were approved. Chairman He is now trying to stop this conflict in accordance with the principle of mediation, and he hopes that Director Yan will mediate to prevent the situation from escalating." Hou also plans to visit Sun's representative Gao Mengqin and Ma's representative Kang Yushu for consultations after visiting Yan. (18th)

Songjiang

The Commissioner's Office is Ordered to Close 87

After the reorganization of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, there have been slight changes in the commissioner system in the province. The thirteen districts have been reduced to nine. For the convenience of suppressing bandits, the commissioners of the districts in the Jiangbei area will remain. The districts in the Jiangnan area will be closed by the end of February, as decided by the provincial government meeting. The Commissioner's Office of this district received an order from the provincial government yesterday, instructing it to close on schedule and hand over to the concurrently serving county magistrates for receipt and reporting. Commissioner Jin has complied with the order. The Fourth District has been renamed Songjiang District and its jurisdiction has been expanded to seven counties. The commissioner does not concurrently serve as the county magistrate. It is currently temporarily closed, but it will still need to be established in the future depending on the situation.

A Robbery Occurs in Longxing, a Suburb Nearby 88

The home of Lu Ziwen in Yujia Village, Longxing Township, about five li north of Bailongtan in this city, was suddenly visited by more than ten bandits on the night of the 22nd. Each held a long or short gun. After entering the house, they ordered the homeowner to hand over the location of the hidden silver. The homeowner begged for mercy, but as a result, a fur coat and more than 30 yuan in cash were robbed. Before leaving, they also stole a small boat. A farmer surnamed So-and-so in the Xiaokunshan Township of the Ninth District was also robbed the night before. The bureau has been notified to investigate.

Suzhou

The Freezing of Rivers Due to Cold Weather Affects Transportation 89

Due to the continuous cold weather, the small river ports are frozen. Seven or eight out of ten ships traveling between Suzhou and the villages have stopped running on the 22nd. Small steamships can still operate, but according to the boatmen, if the thaw does not come, the ice will become thicker and wider, and the shipping will be temporarily suspended. The transportation between the city and the countryside will be greatly affected.

The Civil Affairs Department Sends Personnel to Review the Water Police in Various Districts 90

In order to understand the actual situation of the water police in various districts of Jiangsu Province, the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department has specially dispatched Zhang Jiqun, director of the review team, to review the water police in various districts. Zhang is scheduled to come to Suzhou today (the 23rd) to review the various teams stationed in the Second District of Suzhou-Wuxi. He is scheduled to review the First District on February 1, the Third District on February 9, the Fourth District on February 17, and the Marine Guerrilla Force on February 26.

Wuxi

The Chamber of Commerce Submits the Re-election to the Ministry of Industry for Interpretation 91

The Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce conducted a re-election on the 15th of this month. Prior to this, it received instructions from the Provincial Party Headquarters through the County Party Headquarters, stipulating that if the incumbents on the Executive Committee were elected to the Supervisory Committee, or the incumbents on the Supervisory Committee were elected to the Executive Committee, the re-election of the Chamber of Commerce and trade associations would be invalid. The Chamber of Commerce held that the Chamber of Commerce Law did not expressly stipulate this, and the matter concerned laws and regulations, which could not be interpreted arbitrarily. On that day, it sent telegrams to the Central Party Headquarters, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Industry for interpretation. It received a telegram from the Ministry of Industry, which stated that "The prior question to the aforementioned election situation is whether the Executive and Supervisory Committees can hold concurrent positions. Although the laws and regulations regarding the Chamber of Commerce and trade associations do not explicitly prohibit concurrent positions, the nature of the Executive and Supervisory Committees is that one is the executor of the association's affairs and the other is the supervisor of the execution of the association's affairs, and there is no reason why they can hold concurrent positions. If the elected person is willing to resign from their old position and take up the new position, there is no obstacle. [seal of the Ministry of Industry]." Upon receiving the telegram, the Chamber of Commerce stated that the case had been instructed by the Party Headquarters, and in accordance with Article 10 of the Central Amendment to the General Rules for Elections of People's Organizations, a part of the election was invalid, with three items listed clearly. It did not involve the fact that incumbent members of the Executive and Supervisory Committees cannot elect each other, and it should not be arbitrarily asserted, so as not to disregard the Central Government. Therefore, it sent another telegram to the Ministry of Industry for clear instructions on how to handle the matter, and sent a copy of the original telegram to the Party and government authorities for reference.

Jiaxing

Prosecution of the Woman Who Killed Her Sister-in-Law 92

Miao Ni, a farmer from Yunbei Township, Wangdian, Jiaxing, often quarreled with her sister-in-law, Miao Chen. Recently, Ni, under the influence of alcohol, had another argument with Chen. In the end, she used an iron hoe to smash Chen's skull, resulting in a fatal injury. Subsequently, members of the Miao clan reported the incident to the court. After an investigation by the prosecutor's office, Ni confessed to the fatal blow. A forensic examination confirmed that the injuries inflicted before death were the cause of death. As a result, Prosecutor Wang Bangyan has filed a public prosecution with the criminal court, and a public trial will be held soon.

Hangzhou

American Consulate Car Accident Case 93

Mu Jue, an American consul stationed in Shanghai, drove his own car from Shanghai to Hangzhou along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway on the 11th of this month. When passing through Caojing Station in the Jinshan County area of Jiangsu Province, he ran over and killed a salt worker named Mao Xiaolong. The Road Bureau impounded his driver's license and other documents and reported the incident to the Construction Department of the Provincial Government, which in turn consulted with the Shanghai Municipal Government. As the accident occurred within Jiangsu Province, the entire case file and details of the accident have been transferred to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for investigation.

Huang Xuchu, a member of the Fourth Plenary Session representing Guangxi Province, along with Central Committee member Chen Zhongfu, Chen Jitang, and Yang Dezhao, the representative of Guangxi stationed in Beijing, arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong on the President Cleveland of the Great Eastern Shipping Company yesterday morning at 7:30 a.m. Huang took the night train to Beijing that evening to attend the plenary session. Yang stayed in Shanghai for a short while and will go to Beijing in a few days to meet with Chairman Chiang and report on everything. The details are as follows:

Attending the Plenary Session 95

After arriving in Shanghai this morning (i.e., yesterday morning), he briefly met with friends from Guangxi in Shanghai and then took the night train to Beijing. Southwest's Attitude Towards Fujian 96

When reporters inquired about the Southwest authorities' attitude towards the Fujian issue, he replied that the rebellion in Fujian Province had been resolved, and the issue of incorporating the 19th Route Army would be subject to the central government's orders. Chen Bonan (Chen Jitang) has absolutely no opinion on incorporating the army, and rumors that Chen intends to incorporate the army are inaccurate. As for the reports that the Southwest authorities telegraphed the central government, requesting that it not pursue the defeated Chen Mingshu and Cai Tingkai when the national army captured Fuzhou and they retreated to Zhangzhou and Quanzhou, this is also not true. As far as he knows, the Southwest side did not make such a request. In short, Chen Bonan has no suggestions regarding anything in Fujian Province going forward.

Chen and Li Go Abroad 97

As for Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, and others, they had considerable history and friendship with the leaders of the Southwest before the Fujian Incident. Now that Chen and Li have declared their departure from the Kuomintang and have committed acts of treason against the party and the country, there is no doubt that the Southwest will not allow them to set foot there again. As for Chen Youren, he has no close relationship with the Southwest. In the future, Chen and Li will be discredited and may go abroad.

Suppressing Bandits Continues 98

The Southwest continues to suppress bandits, hoping to eradicate the banditry in Jiangxi Province as soon as possible. They are also proceeding with local construction matters according to their original plans. As for Xiao Focheng, he has requested leave to go to Siam due to old age and poor health, as well as the unsuitable climate of Guangdong for recuperation. The General Labor Union Submitted a Request to the Fourth Plenary Session Yesterday 101

Requesting Explicit Regulations on the Organization of the General Labor Union

Temporary Registration Should Be Permitted Before the Promulgation of New Laws

Dagong News reports: "The Shanghai General Labor Union submitted a request to the Fourth Plenary Session yesterday: '(Omitted above) Requesting a petition to the National Government to instruct the Legislative Yuan to promptly revise the Labor Union Law, explicitly stipulating that each province and city may organize a General Labor Union or promulgate separate organizational regulations for the Shanghai General Labor Union, and requesting the Central People's Movement Committee to provisionally approve the registration of professional associations before the promulgation of the new law, in order to provide relief and facilitate progress. Since the promulgation of the Labor Union Law, the former Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai General Labor Union was canceled due to the restrictions of the law. As a result, the labor movement in Shanghai lost its

Leading Center 102

and fell into a state of division and decline. When the Liaoning Incident suddenly broke out and the national crisis became serious, the labor community in Shanghai, realizing the growing urgency of the national crisis, understood that only sincere unity could save the country and resist foreign aggression. Therefore, the Professional Association, in response to the urgent needs of the environment, was established through the resolution of the city-wide labor representatives' congress. It has been three years since its establishment, and its past work has been remarkable and widely recognized by all sectors. However, due to legal restrictions, there have been many obstacles to its progress. Therefore, in September of last year, a request was submitted to the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters,

Requesting Approval for Registration 103

After careful consideration, the Municipal Party Headquarters considered that the organization of the Professional Association was necessary in light of the circumstances and approved temporary registration on October 2 and reported this to the Central Government. However, the Central People's Movement Committee recently ordered that the name be changed to the "National Salvation Federation of Various Industry Labor Unions" on the grounds that the Professional Association violated the law. Considering its meaning, the work in the future will be subject to strict restrictions. The entire labor community is deeply bewildered. We hereby state the reasons and request the maintenance of the original organization. Since its establishment, the affiliated association has made the greatest efforts to lead the city's labor community in responding to the serious national crisis, and it has achieved significant results in preventing communist activities, resolving disputes in various industries, and promoting cooperation between labor and management. Other efforts include holding labor education lectures, summer labor temporary relief centers, and running labor supplementary night schools, paying attention to the welfare of workers and sparing no effort to seek further progress. Therefore, based on the past achievements, it is necessary to allow it to exist. This is the first reason. The Professional Association, due to its past efforts, has gained deep recognition from all sectors of the city. All

Important Legal Entities 104

recognize that the Professional Association is the only general labor movement group, and the various industry labor unions in the city can convey their fervent belief and unanimously support it. Thus, although the Professional Association is not legally based, it has in fact gained public recognition. This is the second reason for requesting approval to exist. Since its establishment, the Professional Association has exchanged telegrams with various government agencies, and the cases have become numerous. For example, the National Government Civil Service Office, the Executive Yuan, the Judicial Yuan, the Central Propaganda Committee, and the Shanghai Municipal Government have all sent approvals or letters to the association. Last year, the Professional Association, recognizing the importance of aviation construction, raised a large amount of money and donated it to the government. Chairman Lin of the National Government also

Awarded a Citation 105

Thus, although the Professional Association has not obtained legal protection, it has been recognized by government agencies that enforce the law. This is the third reason for requesting approval to exist. In view of the fact that the Central Government allows general organizations for agricultural, commercial, and academic sectors, we, the labor community, are also citizens. Why should we be excluded? This is the fourth reason for requesting approval to exist. In summary, whether in terms of reason or law, the Professional Association needs to exist. Therefore, we have prepared this document to request your review and resolution, approving a petition to the National Government to instruct the Legislative Yuan to promptly revise the Labor Union Law, making sure to

Explicitly Stipulate 106

that each province and city may organize a general labor union or promulgate separate organizational regulations for the Shanghai General Labor Union, and requesting the Central People's Movement Committee to provisionally approve the registration of professional associations before the promulgation of the new law, in order to provide relief and facilitate progress. This is extremely urgent. Respectfully submitted to the Presidium of the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, Shanghai General Labor Union, respectfully submitted."

The Central District Telephone Bureau Is Expected to Be Completed by the End of May 107

Costing More Than 26,000 Yuan

The Central District Branch of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, due to incomplete bidding procedures before the relocation of the municipal government, was unable to be constructed. All central district telephone connections are temporarily handled by the Jiangwan Branch. It is now learned that the Telephone Bureau and Dong Ruihe Construction Company have drafted a plan to build a two-story Western-style building, occupying one mu of land. The design of the building was created by Lu Qianshou, the section chief of the Architecture Department of the Bank of China. The price is 26,750 yuan, and a contract has been signed, with delivery expected four months from the start of construction. The Telephone Bureau has submitted the plan to the Ministry of Communications for review, and construction will begin as soon as the approval is issued, with completion expected by the end of May.

Japanese Cotton Cloth Was Dumped Worldwide Last Year 108

Greatly Affecting the UK

Slight Decrease in China

According to the Nagoya News on the 13th, the British Department of Commerce released a report on cotton cloth exports on the 11th, showing a decrease of 167 million square yards compared to the previous year, totaling only 2.031 billion square yards, due to the impact of Japanese dumping. Japanese cotton cloth exports totaled 2.087 billion square yards last year, with South America, Europe, and Africa being the largest sales regions. South America increased to 65 million square yards, while India decreased to 113 million square yards, and China also decreased by 73 million square yards (due to the anti-Japanese movement). The export volumes to various regions last year are listed below: India: 486 million square yards; China: 52 million square yards; Europe: 236 million; Mediterranean: 184 million; Dutch East Indies: 21 million; Africa: 294 million; Singapore: 26 million; South America: 269 million. China decreased by 73 million compared to the previous year.

Central Propaganda Committee Special Commissioners Wang and Lin Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning 109

Scheduled to Fly to Fujian on the China National Aviation Corporation Flight This Morning

After the outbreak of the Fujian Incident, the Central Propaganda Committee feared that the general public would inevitably be misled and exploited by the rebels. As the punitive expeditionary forces have successively recovered important areas in Fujian, fearing that the people of Fujian Province might be estranged due to the misleading anti-government propaganda, the committee specially appointed Wang Yilin and Lin Zigui of the Propaganda Section as special propaganda commissioners for Fujian to conduct propaganda. Two film stock employees were also sent along. After receiving their orders, Wang and Lin arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday morning and are scheduled to fly to Fujian on the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) flight this morning.

To Be Organized by the Municipal Party Headquarters in Conjunction with the Municipal Government

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Various National Goods Organizations Will Participate

The Propaganda Week Will Start on January 28

The second anniversary of the January 28th Incident, when the Japanese invaded Shanghai, is approaching. Recalling the losses suffered by the citizens at that time, exceeding 150 million yuan, and the countless lives sacrificed, we must commemorate this painful anniversary with solemnity. Today, the enemy still has not abandoned its policy of aggression, and in addition to military force, it is also dumping large quantities of goods on the market, causing significant pressure on politics and the economy. The only way forward is to vigorously promote national goods to benefit the national economy and the people's livelihood. It is learned that the Municipal Party Headquarters will organize an unprecedented national goods propaganda movement starting on the anniversary of the January 28th Incident, in conjunction with the Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the General Labor Union, and various national goods organizations, to arouse public awareness of the need to actively adopt national goods. Two Round Trips Per Week After the New Aircraft Is Installed

There Is Still No News of the Aircraft Testing the Southwest Route Leaving Kunming

China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) planned to open the Southwest Route. Director of the Aviation Department Nie Kaiyi and German pilot Anlisheng were piloting the Zhouxu aircraft to test the route. After mistakenly landing in Lang Son, Annam at the end of the year, the aircraft was released after negotiations and flew to Kunming, Yunnan Province, on the 19th of this month. As of yesterday afternoon, the local company had not received any news of the aircraft leaving Kunming. It is estimated that due to weather conditions, the aircraft will fly from Yunnan to Chongqing and then continue westward to Kangding in preparation for opening the Sichuan-Kangding route. Also, after the No. 16 aircraft of the company crashed into the sea near Zhoushan in mid-November while flying the Shanghai-Guangdong route, the company ordered two large Stinson amphibious aircraft from the United States. The aircraft have been shipped and will arrive in Shanghai tomorrow. After being unloaded and assembled, one aircraft will be added to the Shanghai-Guangdong route and will alternate with the No. 17 aircraft for round-trip flights. At the same time, the Shanghai-Guangdong route will be restored, with two round trips per week. The other aircraft will be used for newly opened routes.

Overseas Chinese in the Philippines Sent a Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Refusing Donations from Chinese Nationals 117

To Be Implemented Starting This Year

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a letter from the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Manila, Philippines, yesterday stating: "We have noted that in recent years, the commercial situation in the Philippines has been deteriorating, and both large and small Chinese businesses are in a precarious state and struggling to survive. However, those coming to the Philippines to solicit donations from the mainland are arriving in droves, even more than before. If this situation is not carefully considered and is allowed to continue without restraint, the currency will flow out and the treasury will become empty, leading to the decline and ruin of businesses. In view of this, our chamber convened a joint meeting on December 5 with the Overseas Chinese Education Association, the Overseas Chinese Charity Association, and the various industry trade associations in order to protect the status of overseas Chinese in the Philippines. The meeting unanimously agreed that it is necessary to sympathize with the difficult times and suspend donations in order to recuperate and benefit commercial operations. It was resolved that, starting next year (i.e., 1934), all those coming from the mainland to solicit donations will be unanimously refused. If necessary, a joint meeting of the above-mentioned organizations will be convened to resolve the issue. Accordingly, we have recorded this and hereby inform you for your reference and request that you forward this information to various agencies and organizations in all areas so that those who wish to go abroad to solicit donations do not come to the Philippines in order to avoid futile trips and wasted time. This is in the spirit of public service."

The Industrial Safety Association Released Last Year's Factory Accident Statistics 119

A Total of 415 People Were Killed or Injured

Losses Exceeded 2.3 Million Yuan

According to the Industrial Safety Association's report, there were a total of 165 factory accidents in Shanghai in 1933, resulting in a total of 415 deaths and injuries and losses of approximately 1.3 million yuan or more. The accident analysis is recorded as follows: (1) Fires: 68 incidents, 13 deaths, 37 injuries, losses of 2 million yuan; (2) Falls: 27 incidents, 21 deaths, 28 injuries; (3) Electrocutions: 22 incidents, 23 deaths, losses of 300,000 yuan; (4) Explosions: 13 incidents, 108 deaths, 155 injuries; (5) Crushing: 11 incidents, 8 deaths, 4 injuries; (6) Strikes: 9 incidents, 8 deaths, 7 injuries; (7) Pressing: 7 incidents, 9 deaths, 5 injuries; (8) Burns: 6 incidents, 4 deaths, 4 injuries; (9) Impact: 1 incident, 1 injury. Total: 165 incidents, 194 deaths, 221 injuries, total deaths 415, total losses 1.3 million yuan. According to the above table, fires were the most frequent type of accident, accounting for 41% of the total, followed by falls, electrocutions, explosions, and crushings. Explosions accounted for the most deaths and injuries, at 58%, followed by floods, falls, electrocutions, strikes, and pressings. Judging from the number of occurrences and the percentage of deaths and injuries, explosions were the most serious, followed by fires. The greatest economic losses for factories were due to fires, followed by explosions.

The Fire Insurance Compensation Coordination Association and the Claims Association Are No Longer Necessary 120

The Bureau of Social Affairs Ordered the Two Associations to Cease Activities

New Sound News reports: "The Fire Insurance Compensation Coordination Association and the Claims Association in the disaster area of this city were established because the insured parties suffered heavy losses during the January 28th battle. They requested the municipal government and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to negotiate for compensation in order to provide relief. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs repeatedly convened meetings on this case and sent personnel to coordinate. However, the bureau believes that the area directly damaged by artillery fire in this city during the January 28th battle was almost half of the entire city, and the citizens who suffered heavy losses were not limited to the insured parties. Although a total of 500,000 yuan in relief funds has been allocated successively for various active relief and temporary emergency relief efforts, it is ultimately a drop in the bucket and cannot solve the problem. It was decided to expand this case to provide relief to general disaster victims in the war zone, so that both insured and uninsured parties in each war zone can enjoy the benefits of relief. The bureau has been soliciting funds from Chinese and foreign organizations for this purpose. As the Fire Insurance Compensation Coordination Association and the Claims Association are now unnecessary, they have been instructed to cease activities."

Report from the Chinese Cotton Statistics Association on the Final Estimate of National Cotton Production 122

Cotton Production Totals 9,621,240 Dan

The Highest Production in the Last Fifteen Years

According to the Kwowen News Agency, the Chinese Cotton Statistics Association recently released its final estimate report on national cotton production for the past year. The details are as follows:

Estimation Process: This estimation is based on reports from (1) eleven provinces, including Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, as well as the two cities of Shanghai and Tianjin; (2) cotton crop conditions before December 10th as the standard; (3) the losses from disasters affecting cotton crops in various provinces before December 10th were all taken into account; (4) cotton fields were measured in Chinese acres (華畝), and cotton production was measured in dan (擔). The estimated results are as follows: cotton field area of 40,453,953 acres, ginned cotton production of 9,621,240 dan, and abandoned field area of 617,398 acres. According to the revised estimate for the 21st year of the Republic (1932), the cotton field area was 37,009,800 acres, and the ginned cotton production was 8,105,637 dan.

Comparison of Two Years: This estimate can now be considered the final actual yield. The 9,621,240 dan represents an increase of 1,515,603 dan compared to the 21st year of the Republic. This high yield is not only unprecedented in recent years but also the largest production figure since the 8th year of the Republic (1919). At a time when domestic cotton production cannot meet demand and huge amounts of foreign cotton are imported, this is a relatively gratifying report. The increase in production is mainly due to the increase in cotton fields. The increase in cotton fields is more significant in the north, as the disturbances caused by soldiers and bandits have subsided somewhat, and farmers can live relatively peacefully. In addition, the weather has been favorable, with ample rainfall, which has led to an increase in cotton fields. The soil in the five provinces of Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Shaanxi, and Shanxi is most suitable for cotton cultivation. If irrigation methods can be developed for farmers and there are no wars, the promotion of cotton cultivation will be very easy. Cotton production in the south is generally higher than in the north. Since the severe floods in Jiangsu and Hubei provinces, which were major cotton-producing areas, in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), cotton production has been greatly reduced. Although there has been recovery in recent years, the rural areas are still not very peaceful. Therefore, the rate of increase in cotton fields cannot keep pace with that in the north.

Overview of Cotton Fields: This year, the area of cotton fields has increased in provinces such as Hebei, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, and Jiangsu, with the most significant increases in Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Hubei, and Jiangsu. Cotton cultivation along the Pinghan Railway in Hebei is developing rapidly. In Shanxi, local conditions have been relatively stable in recent years, and cotton production has been recovering. In Henan and Shaanxi, there have been no wars, and grain prices are low, so cotton fields have increased. Hubei and Jiangsu suffered severe floods in the 20th year of the Republic, which greatly reduced cotton fields, but recovery has been rapid in recent years. Other provinces have also made progress year by year. Therefore, the total area of cotton fields has been increasing over the years. In the spring and summer of this year, there was abundant rainfall in the north, and cotton crops were sown in a timely manner, which is a major reason for the sharp increase in cotton fields in the north this year. However, there was a slight decrease in Shandong, and many fields were flooded by the Yellow River in the autumn. Fortunately, the water receded quickly, and there was not a total loss.

Furthermore, the responsible members of the Nanjing Film Censorship Committee, as central officials in charge of censorship, have repeatedly passed reactionary films, bending the law and deliberately condoning them. It is obvious that they either have ulterior motives or have secretly accepted bribes and cannot escape punishment.
