Yichang and Other Counties in Hubei

Repeatedly Petition for Exemption

The National Federation of Commerce, due to receiving telegrams and letters from the chambers of commerce of Yichang County, Shashi, Hubei Province, Wuwei County, Xiang'an Town, Anhui Province, etc., appealing for exemption from the increased salt tax in order to maintain the people's food supply, yesterday specifically telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, stating: (Titles omitted) "We recently received telegrams and letters from the chambers of commerce of Yichang County, Shashi, Hubei Province, Wuwei County, Xiang'an Town, Anhui Province, which roughly stated: 'The Ministry of Finance telegraphed that from January 1st, the tax payment for all salt will be changed to using new scales, and 17 jin will be temporarily added per dan according to the old scales for collection, which is equivalent to an increase of more than two yuan and nine jiao per dan. The Ministry of Finance had already increased the surtax on salt in western Hubei by one yuan and five jiao per dan last year. Representatives publicly elected by the people of western Hubei went to Beijing to petition, but they were not granted a repeal of the order, nor were they granted any reduction. This time, with the change to new scales, the increase could be as much as two yuan and nine jiao per dan, which is truly unbearable for the people. They have repeatedly petitioned for exemption. In addition to sending separate telegrams to the provincial federation of commerce, we specifically telegraphed your association, earnestly requesting you to strive for this with the Ministry in order to maintain the people's food supply, and we earnestly hope,' and so on. In view of this, we hereby telegraphically report to Your Ministry for your examination and approval. We earnestly request that you consider the people's hardship and exempt them from the increase, which is our most fervent prayer. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, bows his head."

After the Puan Steamer was Robbed, Guangdong and Fujian Have Sent Military Police to Encircle and Suppress (the Pirates) 126

The Ship's Crew's Losses Will Be Compensated by the Bureau

Additional Anti-Theft Equipment Installed on All Vessels

After the Puan steamer of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company returned to Shanghai after being robbed by pirates, it has now sailed to Qingdao as usual. The authorities in Guangdong and Fujian have sent military police to encircle and suppress the pirates and rescue the passengers. Details are as follows:

Encirclement and Suppression of Pirates 127

The Board of Directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has decided to offer a reward of 10,000 yuan for the strict arrest of the pirates who robbed the Puan steamer, and has also telegraphed Chairman Chiang, requesting him to instruct the strict arrest of the pirates and the rescue of the passengers. Yesterday, they received a reply telegram from Chairman Chiang, who has instructed the Guangdong and Fujian provincial governments to order the nearby military police to encircle and suppress the pirates and rescue the abducted passengers. At the same time, the Navy Department has dispatched warships stationed in Xiamen to Zhao'an to encircle and suppress the pirates.

Ship's Crew Losses 128

General Manager Liu Hongsheng has not only sent the passengers who suffered on the Puan steamer to Qingdao free of charge as usual but also provided meals. The Puan steamer has now safely arrived in Qingdao. As for the clothing of the ship's crew, such as Purser Zou Lun, First Officer Sun Zuoren, etc., which was robbed by the pirates, the General Bureau will compensate them according to the loss reports submitted by each crew member to show its concern.

Strict Anti-Theft Measures 129

Since the Puan steamer was robbed, in addition to dispatching guards to escort each vessel of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the river steamers that have not been equipped with radio have been newly equipped with radio. For the ocean-going vessels, anti-theft equipment has been added in accordance with the anti-theft and escort regulations promulgated by the Executive Yuan, such as iron gates installed in the bridge, engine room, and radio room to separate them from the passengers for prevention.

Maritime Steamer Workers of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Went on Strike Yesterday 130

The Steamer Has Been Leased to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Sail to Northern and Southern Ports

The Seamen's Union Sent Representatives to Persuade Them to Resume Work, but to No Avail

According to the New Voice News Agency, all the workers on the Maritime Steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company went on strike yesterday because they opposed the company's unwarranted dismissal of workers and rejected the union's mediation. Details are as follows:

Carrying Smuggled Goods 131

Since the Maritime Steamer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was leased to the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to operate the Shanghai-Qingdao and Shanghai-Guangdong northern and southern routes, the original workers in the middle cabin, cargo handlers, stokers, sailors, and other departments also served on the steamer, but they were still under the jurisdiction of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Unexpectedly, in August last year, some workers on the steamer carried smuggled goods, which were seized by the Guangdong Customs, and they were fined more than 2,000 yuan.

Dismissal of Sailors 132

At that time, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company temporarily paid the fine, and after returning to Shanghai, it turned to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company for reimbursement. However, because the workers could not pay, they paid half each. The workers, on the other hand, sought a guarantor and agreed to pay in installments. Unexpectedly, the company deducted two months' salary from the workers and dismissed more than a dozen sailors from the entire sailor department, including Wang Yongfa and Zhu Shunbao. The other workers were extremely angry that the company deducted their salaries and dismissed them.

Unsuccessful Negotiations 133

After the company dismissed the workers in the sailor department last year, it hired Xu Huimin and other twelve people to fill the vacancies. The old workers who were dismissed petitioned the Seamen's Union to negotiate for their reinstatement. However, after the union repeatedly sent staff members Cheng Deyuan and Gao Shuren to negotiate with the company's manager, Ye Chuanfang, the company ignored them. This month, the branch union took over the negotiations, but it was also ineffective.

Complete Strike 134

The Maritime Steamer arrived in Shanghai from Guangdong at 8:00 AM yesterday and docked at the Yangjiadu Wharf in the Nanshi district. It was originally scheduled to sail to Qingdao today. Unexpectedly, at 3:30 PM, all 68 workers on the steamer, including twelve stokers, thirty-two cargo handlers, twelve sailors, five middle cabin workers, and six pursers, stopped working and declared a strike.

Union Persuasion 135

Upon hearing the report, the Seamen's Union and the Seamen's Branch Union, believing that the case was serious and fearing that it would lead to further complications and affect travelers, sent Cheng Fanyuan from the General Union, together with branch union committee member Lu Rongzhi, to the wharf at 4:00 PM to persuade them to resume work. However, all the workers were very determined, so despite repeated persuasion, it was still ineffective, and the situation was very serious.

The Wanbao Silk Factory Dispute Resolved 136

A Written Record of Three Items Signed Yesterday at the Social Bureau

According to the New Voice News Agency, the Wanbao Silk Factory on Route Sapey in the French Concession, which has a total of 120 workers, had a dispute recently due to the factory's unwarranted reduction of wages. Yesterday, the Social Bureau convened both parties for mediation. The workers' representatives were Gu Yuqing and Xie Yuanlong, and the factory's representatives were Li Mingzhi and Xuan Taihua. The meeting was chaired by Zhu Guilin, a staff member from the Third Section of the Social Bureau. After inquiring about the reasons, both parties reached an agreement and signed a written record of three items on the spot, and the dispute was resolved. The items are: (1) The price of brocade crepe work is reduced to one jiao and three fen and five li per yard, and the price of plain satin is reduced to seven fen per yard; (2) For every four machines, the workers may hire one helper, and the factory will subsidize the helper's wage at two yuan per machine per month for day and night shifts; (3) The above measures will be implemented from today, and they may be restored when the market improves.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Actively Prepares for the Nanshi National Goods Bazaar 137

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce has chosen the original site of the former County Chamber of Commerce to open the Nanshi National Goods Bazaar. Various news about this has been reported in this newspaper. The chamber has now hired workers to renovate the site and has sent staff to design and plan it. They are striving for novelty in terms of form and color in order to suit modern aesthetics. It is also reported that many national goods factories have come to discuss participation, but the chamber, in order to be cautious about the matter, will only select those factories with high-quality products to join.

The French Concession Drastically Restricts Rickshaw Licenses 138

Rickshaw Operators in Nanshi Petition for Assistance from the Taxpayers' Association

Rickshaw licenses in the French Concession used to be freely purchased by rickshaw operators. Since the board of directors decided to limit the number to 17,000, in addition to the 10,000 licenses allocated to the Public Concession, among the remaining 7,000 licenses, due to the rush to purchase licenses in western Shanghai, the rickshaw operators in Nanshi who have fulfilled their tax payment obligations over the years have rickshaws but no licenses, which affects their livelihood and business and makes it impossible for them to maintain their operations. Yesterday, they specifically submitted a petition to the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association, requesting assistance. The original text of the petition is recorded below: "We are submitting this petition to express our grievances and request that the French Municipal Council consider the livelihood of the poor and supplement rickshaw licenses. We, the operators of rickshaw companies in Nanshi, have been operating rickshaws with licenses from the Shanghai Municipal Council and the French Municipal Council for many years. As for the French Concession licenses, in addition to the 10,000 licenses allocated to the Public Concession with designated numbers, there has never been a fixed number in Nanshi. Rickshaw operators freely pay taxes depending on whether business is good or bad, so they can barely maintain their operations with profit and loss adjustments. Unexpectedly, recently, with the bankruptcy of rural areas north of the Yangtze River, there are more and more rickshaw pullers, and rickshaws from Zhabei and western Shanghai have all moved here to operate, resulting in a shortage of the 7,000 rickshaw licenses temporarily stipulated by the French Municipal Council, and the rickshaw operators who have been operating in Nanshi for many years are unable to obtain licenses because they were a little late in paying taxes. They can only sigh in vain. Those rickshaws with only single-sided Chinese licenses can only operate in a limited area in the Chinese territory. There are also many who reside in the French Concession and cannot operate. The suffering suffered by rickshaw operators and rickshaw pullers in the past two months cannot be described in words. Although we are extremely anxious, regarding the temporary regulations of the French Municipal Council, we still hope that it will take into account the actual needs and make proper arrangements for the livelihood of these poor people. Therefore, we have tried our best to comfort the rickshaw pullers and waited quietly for a solution. However, we have been waiting again and again, but there is no hope. We only hear that the French Municipal Council is ordering rickshaw operators who have already paid taxes to go through the formalities of obtaining a guarantee and paying taxes, but it has not heard or asked about the suffering of the rickshaw operators who are eagerly waiting. We, who are suffering from the aftermath of war, are deeply afraid that if the rickshaw business on which we depend for our livelihood is once lost, we will inevitably face the tragedy of our families being displaced. And five or six rickshaw pullers pull one rickshaw, and there are currently about three or four hundred rickshaws without licenses, with about two thousand rickshaw pullers. If we do not find a way to provide relief from this innocent loss, the impact on the future of society will be unimaginable. Moreover, there are records in the tax collection office of the French Municipal Council of the licenses we rickshaw operators have paid for. Even if there are restrictions, they should be carefully considered based on the order of priority. However, without our knowledge, the sudden disruption to our business has caused great obstacles to our operations, and disputes among operators due to unfairness will be inevitable. Therefore, we are submitting this petition to request that Your Association, based on the facts, appeal to the French Municipal Council to pay attention to the livelihood of the poor and allow us, the operators who were temporarily unable to pay taxes, to supplement our taxes in accordance with the records of the tax collection office. We are also willing to comply with the regulations to provide a guarantee and pay taxes and will never delay or resist. This is for the sake of the Municipal Council. Supplementing the taxes is limited and will increase revenue, and the livelihood of our dozens of operators and thousands of rickshaw pullers will be maintained for a while, which is also a measure of adapting to the times. We have always admired Your Association's concern for the livelihood of the common people, and we earnestly ask that you grant our request and provide us with effective assistance. We are infinitely grateful and await your orders. Sincerely submitted to the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association, Rickshaw Operators in Nanshi, Lü Xiushan, Yu Shanjiang, Wang Taikang, Wu Jiufa, Jiang Heshang, Chen Changsheng, Li Pingyu, Liu Qikuan, Zhou Jungong, Zhang Zhengkui, Li Wanzhang, et al."

Robbers of the Yong'an Company Senteenced 139

The Yong'an Company was robbed of more than 18,000 yuan on December 6th last year. At that time, You A'gen, the chief detective of the Laoza Gate Police Station, arrested the main robbers in the case, Yan A'mao, Feng Zuowen, the woman Pan Meimei, and the instigator Hu Songshan, four people in total. One handgun and many bullets were confiscated. They were handed over to the First Special Court, where they were sentenced separately. However, the ringleader Da A'ge and others were still at large. It was not until the 6th of this month that Lu Liankui, the chief inspector of the General Inspection Office, and Detective Liu Shaokui learned that Da A'ge was Lin Yunliang, also known as Xia Liang, from Ningbo, who was hiding at No. 4, Xiaodong's House, Jiangqiao Temple, Xixiang, outside the Ximen of Zhenhai, Ningbo. They ordered Chinese detectives Chen Yonggui and Wu Hanzhang to go there and arrest Lin. At the same time, Lin's brother, Lin Yuncai, was also arrested. They were brought back to Shanghai, and Fang A'di, a principal offender from Pudong, was arrested in Room 144 of the Hongkou Grand Hotel. In total, one handgun, six bullets, and 9,600 yuan of the original stolen money were confiscated. The police station's lawyer, Li Zhishan, filed a public prosecution with the First Special Court in accordance with the law. After the interrogation was concluded, Feng Shide, the head of the criminal court, took his seat in the Criminal Court No. 1 yesterday morning and announced the verdict: Lin Yunliang and Lin Yuncai were each sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment, and Fang A'di was sentenced to thirteen years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment was finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days. The handgun and six bullets were confiscated, and the stolen 9,600 yuan was returned to the victim.

Car and Truck Collide at the Intersection of Hongqiao Road and Zhongshan Road 140

Boy Ma Wenzi Dies from Serious Injuries

Passenger Wang Shaotang Suffers Serious Injuries

Ma Tangshi from Jiangbei, who lives in Yaojiaqiao, Zhabei, purchased a coffin because her husband's brother, Ma A'san, died in Caohejing. She hired a freight truck from the Xinzhapu Bridge, Beihua Bacon Truck Company to transport the coffin to Caohejing. The company sent four workers, and the driver Wu Changsheng from Yancheng (27 years old) drove truck No. 3842. Ma Tangshi also accompanied the truck with her three-year-old boy, Ma Wenzi, in her arms. Unexpectedly, when the truck reached the intersection of Hongqiao Road and Zhongshan Road in western Shanghai, a local resident, Wang Shaotang, who lives in Chengjiaqiao, was riding in a car from the Dongxin Motor Company (driver Zhao Linxiang from Pudong, 28 years old), driving car No. 963, rental license No. 12416, on Hongqiao Road, going from east to west to the intersection of Zhongshan Road. Because both vehicles were driving very fast, they could not avoid each other and collided violently. The engine cylinders of the Dongxin Company's rental car were smashed, and all the parts were destroyed. Passenger Wang Shaotang's head and face were cut by glass, his eyes were protruding, and he was seriously injured. Ma Tangshi, who was standing on the truck, was shocked, causing Ma Wenzi to be thrown from her arms and fall to the ground. Zhou Yida, the police chief of the Hejiajiao Police Station, Second Precinct, Sixth District, arrived upon hearing the news. He first sent the injured boy Ma Wenzi and passenger Wang Shaotang to the Red Cross Hospital on Avenue Haig for treatment. However, Ma Wenzi died from serious injuries upon arrival at the hospital. The car drivers, Wu Changsheng and Zhao Linxiang, were taken to the Second Precinct, Sixth District for questioning. It was found that this area was where the Second Post of Hejiajiao was stationed. Two weeks ago, the post was temporarily withdrawn pending resolution due to the issue of boundary crossing negotiations. Unexpectedly, it was not long before several accidents were reported to have occurred.

Work of the General Assembly of the Seventh-day Adventist Church 141

The China General Conference of Seventh-day Adventists is holding its spring council meeting from the 12th to the 23rd of this month at the church's headquarters on Ningguo Road in this city to discuss this year's work plans for various departments and all administrative plans. In addition to President Dr. Miller and the staff of various departments of the General Affairs Office, there are more than 30 representatives from the East China, West China, South China, North China, Northeast China, and Northwest China Unions. After the end of today's meeting, the representatives will leave for home. The work of the church can be briefly divided into four departments: evangelism, education, medicine, and publications. During this meeting, in addition to the daily business time, there are also reports from each department on the progress of their work over the past year from 7:00 PM to 8:30 PM every night. It is said that although the situation is turbulent and the economy is difficult, the church's service work, relying on the enthusiastic support of people in the country and the efforts of the church's staff, has made considerable progress in the past year. On the 18th, the representatives took a car to Qiaotou Town to attend the board meeting of the China San Yu Institute. In the past two days, they have also repeatedly visited the board meetings of the Shanghai Sanitarium and Health Hospital on Route Robegen and the Signs of the Times Publishing House on Ningguo Road. The China San Yu Institute is a place for training talents for the work of the Seventh-day Adventist Church and is one of the well-known vocational schools in the country, with more than 350 members, most of whom work diligently to support themselves. Its affiliated primary and secondary schools number about 150. All secondary schools have industries to help students support themselves. The Shanghai Sanitarium and Health Hospital aims to serve patients from all walks of life. There are ten branch hospitals throughout the country, and most of the expenses are supported by donations from people in the country. The Signs of the Times Publishing House is the center of the church's literary evangelism work, publishing regular publications such as the Signs of the Times Monthly and dozens of books such as Healthy Living and The World's Hope. There are more than 200 salespersons who sell them throughout the country. Last year's total business volume reached more than 240,000 yuan. The Signs of the Times Monthly has 78,000 subscribers. The Seventh-day Adventist Church's work in China began 30 years ago, founded by Dr. Miller and others in Guangzhou, Henan, and other places. After arduous management, it has made rapid progress. In recent years, it has also used "Go to the frontiers" as its slogan, aiming to spread throughout the country. The church advocates the separation of politics and religion, and its purpose is purely to cultivate believers who are suitable for Christian education, so that individuals, families, society, and the country can all move toward goodness. It is said that there are now more than 12,000 church members.

It is scheduled to be completed on February 10th. It will then notify the Telephone Bureau to handle the cutting of lines. Around February 20th, all telephones in Pudong can be completely transferred to the management of the Telephone Bureau.

Public Notice from the Grain Guild Regarding Rectifying Sampling Practices 144

The Shanghai Grain, Oil Cake, and Allied Trades Association hereby issues a public notice to all fellow businesses: We have received a letter from the Chief of the Second Section of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Police, stating that regarding the matter of merchants sending people to grain stations to take samples, there are points that should be noted regarding procedures. We previously sent a letter notifying you of this and requesting that you inform your fellow businesses to take note. However, it has been found that while many of the samplers sent by various merchants follow the procedures, there are still quite a few who secretly engage in trickery. To protect both customers and goods, in addition to issuing notices to all warehouses and instructing all officers to inspect sample slips at any time, we are hereby sending this letter to you, hoping that you will inform your fellow businesses that from now on, when sending people to the station to take samples, they must carry a formal sample slip, clearly stating the number of the car from which the sample is taken and the name of the goods to be transported. They must not take advantage of the situation to take samples indiscriminately, so as to protect customer interests and facilitate railway transportation. You are hereby notified. All fellow businesses are requested to take note and comply.

Displacement of Waterway Lightship 146

Notice to Mariners from the Hydrographic Office

The Hydrographic Office of the Navy Department has issued a notice to mariners regarding the displacement of the Haibeigang Sand Waterway Lightship at the mouth of the Yangtze River on the East Coast, urging mariners to take note.

(Date of Change) Approximately January 23 of this year. New position: Bi tiee, 85 degrees true north from the east of Longtan Port, a distance of 1.59 nautical miles, i.e., approximately 120 degrees 27 minutes east longitude, and approximately 32 degrees 3 minutes north latitude. Note: "Pay attention to the upper section of the west entrance of Haibeigang Sand." The lightship will be moved to the above-mentioned new position, and its nature remains the same. (Related Maps) Navy Department Hydrographic Charts Nos. 143 and 144. (Reporting Agency) Shanghai Customs. (Note) The directions given in this notice to mariners are calculated from 0 degrees true north, turning clockwise to 359 degrees. However, the direction of the light is calculated from the sea. The brightness and distance of the light are based on clear weather conditions. The fog signal is only used in foggy weather and will be specified separately if necessary. The depth measurements are based on the largest scale chart and calculated using the reference plane.

Shipping Companies Hold Anti-Piracy Conference 150

Officials from the Water and Land Police Departments Attended

Five Anti-Piracy Measures Resolved

Since the Executive Yuan promulgated the "Escort and Anti-Piracy Regulations," all shipping companies have complied with them. A special anti-piracy conference was held the day before yesterday to discuss anti-piracy measures. The details are as follows:

Representatives from various shipping companies attended the anti-piracy conference at the Shipping Club on the fourth floor of 10 Guangdong Road at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. Attendees included Yu Kekai from Ning Shao Company, Chen Yixian from Ping An Company, Zhou Bolun from Mao Li Bureau, Yang Guanbei and Yang Qingbang from Dada Company, Luo Lianchen from Huxing Company, Feng Zhongfang from Dayuan Company, Cao Qiming from Jufeng Binji Company, Mao Youren from Datong Renji Company, Chen Yisheng from Lian An Company, and Mao Youren from Dazhen Company. Zhu, the captain of the Water Patrol, Guan, the chief of the First District, Officer Guo, Gao, the deputy director of the Dock and Warehouse Management Office, and over twenty other people attended.

Measures Resolved: Chen Yisheng chaired the meeting and reported the purpose of the meeting. Then, discussions began. According to a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, the following matters were resolved: (A) For all ships berthed at the Nanshi Wharf, one hour before weighing anchor, the water police, accompanied by female inspectors, the ship's purser, and the accounting office or inspectors, will inspect the passengers. If passengers disembark at that time, the land police stationed at the wharf next to the ship will carry out the inspection to avoid omissions. The inspection rules will be determined separately. (B) The Dock Management Office will send a list of the departure dates and times of all ships to the water and land police agencies. (C) Each shipping company will prepare its own badges to be issued to all crew members, who must wear them. The names, positions, and badge styles of employees must be submitted to the Shipping Association by a deadline, which will then be forwarded to the water and land police agencies for filing. During inspections, anyone who is neither a passenger nor wearing a badge will be immediately expelled from the ship and taken ashore by the water police. Violators will be arrested and punished. (D) Because there are many ships departing at the same time, more police officers should be dispatched to carry out inspections. The expenses will be shared by the shipping companies. The amount of each company's share will be determined by the Shipping Association, which will send a letter to each company to obtain their agreement before implementation. The funds will be collected monthly by the Association and forwarded to the water and land police agencies for distribution. The uniforms and equipment for the newly recruited water and land police will be prepared and distributed by the water and land police agencies. (E) The First District will dispatch more plainclothes detectives to patrol the docks. The above resolutions will be sent by the Shipping Association to all companies and the water and land police agencies.

Recent Conditions of Inland River Transportation in the Severe Cold 151

Laogang Reopened

Inland Rivers Frozen

Suzhou Creek Open to Navigation

Suzhou Creek is a key artery for inland river transportation. Several days ago, due to low tides, civilian freighters coming to Shanghai from various places were congested, blocking traffic three times in succession. From the Banqiao Xinqiao Candle Factory to the Lao Zha Bridge, the river was blocked by ships, preventing civilian freighters from traveling to and from the area for over ten days. At the height of the congestion, even American wheat freighters carrying barges could not load or unload. Subsequently, the water police took measures to drive them away, and inland river steamers changed their routes to the outer rivers. After several days of dredging, navigation resumed on the 20th. Freighters blocked outside and civilian freighters stuck in Laogang have begun to resume traffic yesterday. Many small steamers from various places have also changed their routes to the inner harbor lines.

Freezing Inland: Shanghai has experienced unusually cold weather in recent days, with temperatures dropping sharply and falling to around 20 degrees at night. The highest temperature is also around 37-38 degrees. The climate in Suzhou, Wuxi, Liyang, and Changzhou is even colder than in Shanghai. Reports received in this city yesterday indicated that inland rivers north of Suzhou are covered in thick ice, making navigation for small steamers extremely difficult. Although the waterways have not been completely frozen, small steamers passing through the area are already breaking the ice to proceed, causing delays in scheduled trips since yesterday. Several scheduled trips failed to arrive in Shanghai yesterday. However, according to Yuantong Company and others, the blocked small steamers should be able to reach Shanghai today. As for steamers traveling on the Shanghai-Hangzhou line to Huzhou and other places, they are operating normally without any problems.

Two Firecracker Workshops Exploded 152

White Smoke Filled the Air, Sounds Like a String of Pearls

Three Injured, One False Alarm

Tang Bohai, a 39-year-old from Taizhou, Jiangbei, runs a children's firecracker workshop at 8 Renyifang, Meijia Lane, in the city of Nanshi. Because the Lunar New Year is approaching, the sales of these firecrackers are quite high. Therefore, he recently hired additional workers to work day and night to rush production, so as not to have a shortage of supply during the New Year. Until the night before last, he had produced more than forty plates of firecrackers, totaling about four to five thousand. Because the workshop space was narrow, he temporarily piled them on a table. Unexpectedly, at 6:15 AM yesterday morning, one of the workers accidentally dropped a firecracker on the ground. It made a sharp noise, and sparks ignited the pile of gunpowder raw materials, causing an immediate explosion. With a thunderous sound, over four or five thousand firecrackers exploded simultaneously. The sound was like a string of pearls. At that time, it was just dawn, and nearby residents were awakened from their sleep. At first, they suspected that bandits were shooting to resist arrest. After investigation, they learned the truth. The patrol police of the 1st District, 3rd Precinct, had already reported the incident to the station chief. Chief Jin immediately dispatched a large number of officers to investigate. The sound of the explosion had just subsided, but white smoke filled the surrounding area, shrouding the entire house. It was found that the roof, walls, and mezzanine of the house at number 8 were completely destroyed by the explosion. An eight-year-old child, Xiao Mao, who lived on the mezzanine, suffered serious eye injuries. The front of the Shenchang Copper Shop at numbers 6 and 7 across the street was also blown down. Coppersmiths Zhou Zhengcai and Wu Xiaohu were both injured in the explosion. In addition, the partition walls and mezzanine of number 9 next door also collapsed. Only number 10 suffered minimal damage. After Chief Jin completed his investigation, he took the shop owner, Tang Bohai, into custody for questioning. He also learned that a similar incident occurred at the fuse workshop at noon on the 16th of this month, but it did not cause a major disaster. Chief Jin instructed the police to send the three injured people to the hospital for treatment, pending investigation and punishment.

At around 12:00 PM yesterday morning, a firecracker workshop opened by local Li Yuelin at 5 Xiqing Lane, Sanpailou, in the city, also exploded when a splash of kerosene fell into the firecrackers. Li and his friend Tang Xun were both injured and sent to the hospital for treatment. The 1st District, 2nd Precinct, is currently investigating.

Robbery and Murder at the Zhenyu Goods Factory 153

Thirty Bandits Arrived Together

Tang Xiangshou Died from Three Gunshot Wounds

There have been frequent robberies in the Gonghe Xin Road and Zhongxing Road area of Zhabei recently. At 3:45 AM yesterday morning, another robbery occurred at the Zhenyu Goods Factory on the north side of Zhijiangmiao Road, Gonghe Xin Road. The factory owner, Tang Xiangshou, resisted the bandits and was shot three times, resulting in his death. The details are as follows:

Factory Inspection 154

The Zhenyu Goods Factory is located on the north side of Zhijiangmiao Road, Gonghe Xin Road, facing east. The factory site covers more than ten acres, with addresses from 914 to 930, totaling seventeen rooms. The factory buildings number dozens. Apart from the northern municipal housing, half of which is rented out to others to open cloth factories, the southern part is used for operating factories. The south, west, and north sides of the houses are surrounded by very high bamboo fences. Usually, the factory enters and exits through the small gate along the road on the south side. However, the surroundings of the factory, except for the northern cloth factory, are all open space, so the location is very desolate.

Robbery Situation 155

At 3:45 AM yesterday morning, Tang and his family, partners, and apprentices, totaling more than thirty people, were all asleep. Tang was sleeping alone in a small room on the second floor facing south near the road. His sons and daughters-in-law were in the room opposite Tang's small room. The bandits climbed over the bamboo fence on the south side and pried open the second-floor window to enter Tang's bedroom. Tang heard the noise and woke up to see four bandits standing in front of his bed. Tang usually kept a wooden stick beside his bed. Seeing the bandits arrive, he resisted with the wooden stick and shouted loudly. The bandits immediately fired three shots. One shot hit Tang's left hand, with the bullet exiting from the palm. One shot hit next to his left nipple, with the bullet exiting from his back. One shot hit his left waist, with the bullet remaining in his abdomen. He immediately fell to the floor in a pool of blood. Seeing that they had killed the owner, the bandits immediately overturned boxes and cages, robbing dozens of silver dollars. Still dissatisfied, they went to Tang's daughter-in-law's bedroom to search. Tang's daughter-in-law happened to be in confinement after childbirth. Seeing that she was wearing a gold ring on her hand, they took it off her finger. Downstairs, they saw nothing else worth taking, so they opened the front door and fled. When Tang's family discovered what had happened, they ran to the Tanjiaqiao Branch of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau to report. Police were dispatched to investigate, but the bandits were nowhere to be found. Subsequently, the station reported the situation to the Fourth District, instructing Wang Shaoting, the local constable of the Second Tu, to report to the Shanghai Local Court and request an autopsy.

Autopsy Process 156

At around 3:00 PM, the court dispatched prosecutor Li Fen, accompanied by a clerk and forensic staff, to the scene. It was determined that the deceased, Tang Xiangshou (the constable reported Tang Xiangyou), had indeed been shot and killed. The coroner filled out the corpse form and handed it over to the deceased's family for collection, pending the arrest of the murderers.

Brief Biography of the Deceased 157

Tang Xiangshou was from Dinghai and was fifty years old. He had two sons. The eldest son, Zhencang, is married and works at the Commercial Press. The second son is Zhenhan. Tang himself opened the Deren Paper Mill at 914 Nan Shan Li, Gonghe Road, Zhabei. Because Tang was good at business, he accumulated great wealth over the years. He also had frequent dealings with a certain foreigner due to business relationships. The factory's Zhenyu Goods Distribution Office is located at Wuma Road, Public Concession. As for the truth behind this murder, it is still unclear.

Four Righteous Men Making Trouble for Four Female Performers 158

Trouble Caused by Righteous Men at Pudong Grand Theater

Various Anecdotes from the "Spinning Cotton" Play

Since the Pudong Grand Theater on Yi Du Road, Pudong, hired the entire cast of male and female actors from the former Gengxin Stage to perform the continuous play "Journey to the West," the audience has been filling the theater every day. Among them are four female performers, Zhang Yuqin, Zhou Yanqiu, Mei Yanfang, and Bi Yuezhu, who are all excellent in both appearance and acting skills. They play the role of fairies in the play and are quite beautiful. At 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, four people identifying themselves as "righteous men" suddenly delivered four complimentary tickets, which were handed over to Zhou Zhiliang, the ticket seller of the theater, to be passed on to the four performers, inviting them to a banquet at the nearby Da Zhonghua Restaurant. The four performers, upon receiving this strange note, were unsure who these so-called "righteous men" were. They all ignored it. After about an hour, the so-called "righteous men" sent someone to the theater to urge them. The families of the four female performers believed that they were young and should not engage in unnecessary social interactions. Bi Yuezhu's father replied on the invitation note refusing the invitation. The inviters became angry out of humiliation. They first got drunk at the restaurant and then went to the theater together. They booked eleven private boxes, sat down, and made trouble. Every time any one of the four female performers went on stage, the eleven of them would either shout "Bravo!" in strange voices or hurl filthy abuse. The director of the theater, Gu Shuren, tried to persuade them to stop, but they would not listen. He reported to the 3rd District Police Station, which sent officers to post notices on the walls prohibiting shouting "Bravo!" However, the noise continued as before, with no effect. After the play ended late at night, these eleven people still lingered and would not leave. When the four female performers came out, they all shouted abusive remarks, claiming that they would "give them something to see in three days." The four performers were panicked. The incident was learned by Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the 3rd District. Believing that these people were causing trouble in the theater, affecting the theater's business, and disturbing public order, he sent police to investigate the Da Zhonghua Restaurant. It was learned that Zhou Qilin (31 years old), a Dongtai native working as a translator at the Taikoo Huatong Warehouse, was the ringleader, gathering Wang Yuelou, nicknamed "Little Wang," who works at a foreign company, and others, to deliberately provoke the four female performers. The reason was that when a certain performer sang "Spinning Cotton" a few days ago, Zhou happened to be watching from the audience. When the wife in the play said that her husband had been away for three years and returned to find her holding a child, the husband asked his wife who the child belonged to. The wife replied that it was raised by the neighbor, A San. Upon hearing this, Zhou stood up and shouted, "The neighbor, A San, is me!" This one sentence caused the entire audience to burst into laughter. The performer was quite quick-witted and turned the tables on Zhou, saying that the neighbor A San was the child she was holding. Zhou was speechless and turned red in the face before leaving. Afterwards, he gathered his friends to take revenge. District Chief Zhang believed that his molestation of the female performer was extremely hateful. That night, he sent police to Zhou's residence at 3 Mujia Ferry, took Zhou to the district, and summoned Zhou Zhiliang, the ticket seller, to testify. The district chief severely reprimanded him and sentenced him to fifteen days of detention as a warning.

Children's Welfare Association to Hold Annual General Meeting 160

Scheduled for 4:30 PM on the 29th

Discussing Key Proposals such as the Five-Year Work Plan

The Chinese Children's Welfare Association is scheduled to hold its annual general meeting at 4:30 PM on the afternoon of the 29th of this month at the Zhongshan Hall, 20 Bowuyuan Road. Invitation letters have been sent out, totaling more than 500 copies. Mr. Xu Shiying will be invited to give a speech. Shanghai National Products Company Implements Second Plan 161

Completing the Work of Creating Purchasing Power

The Shanghai National Products Company, located across from the Hongmiao Temple on Nanjing Road, has been experiencing increased business since the early implementation of its second plan. Starting from January 6th, in order to promote the "Women's National Products Year" campaign, in addition to a uniform 10% discount on all goods, it also selects low-priced and high-quality national products every morning, with a specified time and department allocation method, to introduce sacrificial promotions to women. Not only are the prices unprecedentedly low, but the exquisite quality of the goods is also widely praised. As a result, women from all walks of life who love national products are rushing to visit in the mornings. There is a tendency to concentrate the original afternoon purchasing power in the morning. Sometimes the prepared low-priced and high-quality goods are not enough to supply demand, so goods vouchers are issued to ensure that no customer who arrives during the limited time is disappointed, thus further enhancing its reputation. According to Mr. Ren Jinping of the company, attracting purchasing power and creating purchasing power are the secrets of running a business. This time, the company does not hesitate to make significant sacrifices, not only to arouse the concept of loving national products among women, but also to create morning purchasing power. The work of creating time-based purchasing power as defined in the second plan can be said to have been completed.

Man Freezes to Death in Zhabei Due to Severe Cold 162

The recent severe cold weather has led to the frequent deaths of impoverished people from freezing. After being reported by the police officer on duty at Post 18 of the 5th District Public Security Bureau, District Chief Jin Gong sent a patrol officer to investigate and ordered the local constable to report to the court for an autopsy.

Detailed Account of the Kidnapping of Steel Tycoon He Boyan 163

Originated from the Idea of Fugitive Bandit Leader Chen A'liu

Days Spent Observing His Appearance and Movements

Bandits Initially Demanded a Ransom of 300,000

Two Negotiations Yielded No Satisfactory Results

| Court Hearing Postponed to Reschedule After Seven Days |

Steel tycoon He Boyan, who lives at 4 Donghua Lane, Xizang Road, was kidnapped at 10:15 AM on December 27th of last year. He had just left his home and boarded his private car when he was suddenly ambushed by kidnappers. The kidnappers sent a letter demanding a huge ransom. Chief Inspector Shao Jingfan and detectives Wang Youshan, Liang Yuliang, Tao Afu, and Gao Yuqing of the Huizhong Police Department successively apprehended Zhang Aqin and 17 other male and female kidnappers at the Tongyi Hotel on Beihai Road and 1 Zhongde Lane, Longhua Xiaomuqiao Road, on the 13th of this month. He Boyan was rescued, and a pistol and seven bullets were confiscated. They were sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation. It was ordered that the defendants Zhang Aqin, Yang Aqin, Zhang Azhang, Gu Afu (Gu Deming), Yang Shanli, Ji Deming, Lu Yingfan, Huang Jinlong, Zhang Dexing, Tao Changshan, Lu Asan, and 11 others be detained, Gu Daishi and Liu Xiaomao were released on bail, and Zhou Guilin, Su Xiaomei, Lu Shishi, Zhu Xiuying, and Wang Fenggui were released as they were found to have no involvement in the case. It has now been learned that the police

Completed the Investigation Procedures 164

Therefore, this morning, all those in custody were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Defendants Huang Jinlong and Gu Afu hired attorney Fan Gang to represent them in court. Police attorney Jiang Baolian rose to declare that it has been found that defendant Tao Changlin is also not involved in the case and should be released. The court approved this request. Attorney Jiang then detailed the investigation of the case over the past week, stating that the Municipal Council, with the exception of Yang Shanli, is prosecuting all reports under Article 371, Section 1 of the Criminal Code, kidnapping for ransom, and Article 1 of the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits. Yang Shanli, as a tea server at the Tongyi Hotel, is suspected of providing information and is therefore charged with helping to kidnap and extort money. All defendants confessed to the kidnapping in the police station, and their statements have been recorded. The escaped bandit leader Chen A'liu, alias Xiaomao Yujintao, is quite friendly with Gu Afu. Three months before the incident, Chen and Gu met in Baxianqiao. Chen said that he had been having bad luck gambling recently and had incurred heavy debts that he could not repay. He wanted to

Conduct a Kidnapping for Ransom 165

If he could get the ransom money, he could not only pay off his debts but also get a huge amount of money for himself. Gu listened and expressed his agreement. Chen then instructed Gu to go to the Tongyi Hotel on Beihai Road with him. There, they saw the defendants Zhang Aqin, Yang Aqin, Ji Deming, Zhang Dexing, and Lu Asan. They then began a meeting. As a result, they all agreed to the kidnapping. Chen A'liu revealed that the victim's name was He Boyan, who was very wealthy and traveled by car, and was worth a large sum of money. If they did not believe him, they could go to the door of the Far Eastern Hotel the next morning (to identify his appearance). After the discussion, they dispersed. The next morning, ... they were divided near the Far Eastern Hotel. They saw a car with the license plate number 3496 parked at the entrance of the alley. Chen A'liu said to the defendant Lu Asan, "Can you drive this kind of Morris car?" Lu replied that he could. Shortly after, a young man in a suit (He Boyan, the victim in this case) came out of the alley and got into the car. Chen said to Gu, "That's He Boyan."

Are You Seeing Clearly? 166

Then they dispersed immediately. Ten days later, these people opened room number 218 at the Far Eastern Hotel. The signatory was Zhang Dexing. This location was conveniently located opposite the Donghua Lane where the victim, He Boyan, lived, thus allowing them to observe He Boyan's every move. They stayed for about two nights, but due to the high expenses, they couldn't afford it. They then changed to the Unified Hotel, registered under the name of Gu Deming in the circulation book. At the same time, they continued to send people to secretly investigate He's movements every day. Later, they moved to room number 20 in the Shenzhou Hotel and held another meeting, deciding to take action on December 27th.

Preparing to Carry Out the Kidnapping 167

They prepared a letter in advance, addressed to He's father, which roughly stated, "Your son has now joined our party and is being treated very well, please rest assured." They handed it over to Lu Asan for safekeeping and appointed Lu as the driver. Chen then took out three guns, and Zhang Aqing, Yang Aqing, and Ji Deming each took one. At nine o'clock on the morning of the 27th, they all departed from Shenzhou.

Zhang and Ji stood to the left and right of the entrance to Donghua Lane, while Yang and Lu guarded the opposite side. Chen took on the role of patrolling the road. Around ten o'clock, He Boyan left his house and just got into his car. The group immediately stepped forward, threatening him with guns and forbidding him from making any noise. Lu Asan, as the driver, and Ji Deming supervised He's chauffeur, sitting in the front. In the back were the defendants Zhang Aqing and Yang Aqing, who watched over He Boyan. They started the engine and sped forward. After traveling about sixty yards, Lu handed the prepared letter to He's chauffeur and kicked him out. They drove from the French Concession into the Chinese territory, stopping at Small Wooden Bridge Road. At that time, Chen Aliù was already waiting there, with a rickshaw and a cotton quilt prepared. They immediately carried He onto the rickshaw, covering him with the quilt. If they were questioned along the way, they could claim that

The Person in the Quilt is a Patient 168

Who was going to Shanghai for medical treatment, thus avoiding trouble. Later, the rickshaw arrived at Shende Lane. They got out of the rickshaw and entered the alley, helping him into the pavilion room inside the bandit den at number one. They assigned people to guard him, taking turns without rest. After several days, they forced He Boyan to write a letter to his family demanding a ransom. He then wrote a letter to his colleague, He Zhengxiang, asking him to help negotiate. The gang then notified He Zhengxiang by phone, arranging a meeting on the Bund, using a newspaper as a sign. However, He forgot to bring the newspaper, so they didn't meet. Later, they changed the meeting place to the entrance of Jing'an Temple. The defendants Zhang Aqing and Yang Aqing went to meet He and

Demanded a Ransom of 300,000 169

Yuan. He said that He Boyan's family was not wealthy and could not raise such a huge sum. If it was around 10,000 yuan, they could find a way. Because the two sides were too far apart, there was no result, and they dispersed. It wasn't until the 13th of this month that the police cracked the case, rescued the hostage, and seized dark glasses and all the evidence. Now the case has been investigated and concluded, but there is fear that there may be other cases, so they requested permission to postpone the trial again, etc. Then they presented the seized evidence of guns and ammunition to the court. After Judge Xue Lanru questioned the witnesses, including the tea servant of the Unified Hotel, he ordered all the defendants to be returned to custody to await another trial in seven days.

Verdict on the Petty Daily Accusation Case 170

Defendant Huang Guangyi is Not Guilty

The Petty Daily in this city has been published for eight years. Unexpectedly, recently, due to the publication of a long novel, "The Secrets of the Liquor Market," Huang Guangyi, who is financially responsible for the newspaper, was sued by Kuang Yanqi, a fellow townsman who runs a foreign liquor store. The case was heard by Judge Qiu Huan'ying of the Second Special District Court, and two hearings were held on the 13th and 18th of this month. Huang hired three lawyers, Luo Jiaheng, Tang Mingshi, and You Zhi, for defense. Kuang Yanqi claimed that the novel "The Secrets of the Liquor Market" published in the Petty Daily contained the protagonist Guang Asan, also known as Yanqi, who runs the Xingjian Liquor Store, and various family secrets and scandals, which in fact alluded to his name and family history. After publishing dozens of chapters, he entrusted his relative, Jin, to mediate unsuccessfully. Later, he received a letter from Jin stating that he wanted me to donate 500 yuan for charitable donations and publish an apology in the newspaper, etc. He presented Jin's letter as evidence and also filed a private lawsuit through a lawyer, seeking compensation for losses and requesting the court to issue an emergency injunction to order the Petty Daily to immediately cease publishing this novel. However, Kuang stated during the first hearing that everything described in "The Secrets of the Liquor Market" was based on his own facts, but during the second hearing, he claimed that there were no such facts, etc. Huang Guangyi stated during the first hearing that the Petty Daily's text was managed by the editorial department, and the editor-in-chief was You Yi'an. The source of the novel should be questioned from the editor-in-chief. Regarding Jin's mediation, he knew nothing about it. This Jin is Kuang's relative by marriage, and he hasn't seen him for two years. There has been no correspondence during these two years, so how could this have happened? It is clear that Kuang and Jin colluded to frame him. Regarding this letter, please have the court keep it on file, and he will pursue it according to the law. You Yi'an also stated that "The Secrets of the Liquor Market" was the work of the contributor Zhu Taibai. As a novelist, how could he possibly fabricate and forcibly point to allusions? As the editor-in-chief of the Petty Daily, he also reviewed the manuscript and knew that it was a fictional work and had no effect at all, so he published it. If it is as Kuang said, then if someone wants to make things difficult for a novelist in the future, they only need to admit that they are the person described in their writing, and they can file a lawsuit. Then the novelist's castles in the air and playful writing will be in danger of facing criminal charges at any time, etc. The defendants' agents, Tang Mingshi and You Zhi, also used their eloquence to request a verdict of not guilty for Huang Guangyi based on legal facts and to dismiss the private lawsuit attached by the plaintiff. Judge Qiu announced that the verdict would be announced on the morning of the 22nd, and Kuang Yanqi's second request to stop publishing the novel was not approved. At ten o'clock yesterday morning, Judge Qiu ascended to the criminal court and announced the verdict, ruling Huang Guangyi not guilty and dismissing the civil lawsuit attached by Kuang Yanqi. It is reported that Huang Guangyi has filed a private lawsuit against Kuang Yanqi for filing a lawsuit without cause, fabricating evidence, and damaging his reputation, requesting that Kuang be punished for the crimes he deserves. The trial should begin soon.

Robbery on Tangshan Road 171

Yesterday at around 3:20 PM, two bandits suddenly came to a certain family's home at No. 364 Tangshan Road. One bandit had a pistol, and the other guarded the door. They first locked all the people in the house in one room and then began to search separately. However, this family had no savings, so they were only robbed of 80 yuan in paper money and then fled. Afterwards, the victim reported to the competent police station requesting an investigation.

Page 13

Yangshupu Robbery Case Still Awaiting Detailed Investigation 172

The cigarette and paper shop established by Qi Guangrong of Taixing at No. 105 Yangshupu Road was suddenly invaded by three bandits at about 8 o'clock the night before. One held a fake pistol to scare the shop assistants and prevent them from making noise, and two others were on the lookout outside. They were robbed of

Paper money and silver coins, totaling eighteen yuan. As a result, Qi captured one of the bandits and frantically blew the police whistle. Chinese detective Zhou Kaiwen arrived and took him to the Huishan Police Station. Upon interrogation, he confessed that his name was Wang Desheng (from Qingkou). A fake pistol was found in his bag. The police chief ordered him to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Criminal Division 3 of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the defendant admitted at the police station that he came to Shanghai from Pudong and met two fugitives, Zhang Da and Da Lazi. Da Lazi gave him a fake pistol and they went to rob together. These two were the two bandits on the lookout. The wooden fake gun was presented for inspection. Then, according to the victim Qi Guangrong's description of the incident, he was questioned by the defendant, who suddenly recanted, saying that everything he confessed at the police station was nonsense. He and Qi Guangrong had known each other for a long time. He specialized in buying small goods from thieves in the Huangpu River and often hired his boat to transport them. Recently, he bought a large amount of broadcloth, beer, and other items, which he also helped to load, promising to give him a large sum of money. Therefore, he went to settle accounts with him at that time, and a dispute arose. He was accused of being a robber. He spoke eloquently and cried out for injustice, asking the court to see clearly. Qi Guangrong claimed that he did not know him and denied everything. Police lawyer Wang stated that according to the defendant's confession, everything was vividly described. For the sake of caution in this case, he requested that Wang and Qi be jointly detained for detailed investigation, etc. Judge Liu Yugui approved this and ordered the case to be adjourned for investigation and verification.

Central Bank Inspection Report 174

No. 185

The Central Bank's 185th Issuance Reserve Inspection Report states: This committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the banknotes issued by this bank in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations. The 185th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on January 20, 1934. The results of the inspection are hereby announced as follows: (A) Total amount of banknotes issued, 69,151,798 silver dollars, including 63,100,841 silver dollar notes and 6,043,457 subsidiary currency notes. Total amount of banknote reserve fund, 69,151,798 silver dollars, including cash reserve of 56,321,798 silver dollars. The cash reserve included 53,200,2172 dollars stored in the bank's issuing vault, 1,348,148 dollars stored in branches in various ports, and 1,771,478 dollars stored in the same industry. Guaranteed reserve, equivalent to 12,830,000 silver dollars. (B) Customs Gold Banknotes, total amount issued, 416,715.40 yuan. Total amount of Customs Gold Banknote reserve fund, 416,715.40 yuan. This reserve fund includes 6,995 taels, 3 mace and 9 fen of gold, which, at a fixed price of 5957, equals 416,715.40 Customs Gold dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Banknote Regulations, cash reserves are 60% and guaranteed reserves are 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60%, and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. January 22, 1934, Li Fusun, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Supervisors Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiqin.

(2) If the facts are true, the association's legal advisor, Qian Shusheng, will be promoted to handle the case in accordance with the law. (3) Zhou Yanghao, Xu Shengshen, and Yu Denghuai were dispatched to visit the Red Cross Hospital on Haige Road. (4) The association will find a way to maintain the current living conditions of Sun's mother. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Reader Q&A

Reading Plan (4) 186

｜Reply to Mr. Huang Xiuzhong｜

If, as stated in your letter, your purpose in studying history is "to understand the past conditions of present society, so that I may understand why present society is the way it is," and you further wish not to become a "history expert," then undoubtedly the research steps in your plan are unsuitable. Because the approach you are taking is precisely the method of entry for experts, which is unnecessary for the average person. In other words, you don't need to go so far. For the purpose you have, there is another correct research path.

The shortcomings of the research steps you have taken have already been mentioned in your letter, but these are only preliminary, difficulties in terms of material conditions. As for whether you can truly achieve your goal and avoid the problems of "disorder and lack of system" even if you continue to research in this way with great effort, you have not considered it. However, we dare to predict that this situation is inevitable and will only make you feel more unable to research. Because learning must first have a correct method, and without this, one is bound to be "dazzled" and "unable to focus."

If your purpose in studying history is truly as stated in your letter, then we would like to offer another approach.

What you wish to know is the current practical activities of society, and therefore you want to study the development process of human practice. We believe that you do not need to go around in circles, studying from ancient times to the recent past, but rather you should start studying from the recent past and trace back to ancient times. Because if you proceed from top to bottom, you will first spend a lot of time solving many tool-related obstacles. From the perspective of someone who does not engage in specialized research, this is very uneconomical. But this is only uneconomical. If you waste a lot of time and the obstacles still exist, you might abandon the desire to read due to choking, which is not only uneconomical but simply a waste. Moreover, the more ancient the era, the less the influence on later generations and the simpler the relationships. Therefore, the study of ancient times is time-consuming and yields little benefit, which is very uneconomical for amateur self-learners.

In addition, your goal in studying history is only to gain a deeper understanding of reality, which can be achieved by starting research from reality. When you encounter something whose cause-and-effect relationship is unclear, then you can trace back to its cause. Therefore, we believe that when you begin your preliminary research, you can first study various problems. For example, if you wish to study political history, you do not need to start by reading books like *Zizhi Tongjian*. Instead, you should start with various recently occurring facts that you have seen and heard, such as the political situation in recent years, the Northern Expedition of the Kuomintang, Cao Kun's bribery, and then trace back to the Xinhai Revolution. By examining the origins and causal relationships in these events, your concepts will naturally be more accurate and clearer. This method can save a lot of energy for us amateurs. We do not advocate using a vertical method for reading but a horizontal method. This is not only our advocacy for history but for any subject. Because if you study from the present to the past, it is a gradual method of progressing from shallow to deep, peeling back layers. Moreover, phenomena that are close to current life are also the easiest to feel interested in when studying. In amateur self-study, reading is often interrupted. If you use a "horizontal" method, it is like making a small tool; you complete one when you make one. The vertical method is different; it is like a large project, and you cannot achieve success until you have worked for a considerable period. Therefore, for general readers, we strongly hope that they adopt this method, and even those who want to do specialized research can gain many conveniences by starting with this method and then doing further research. Mr. Lü Simian said, "In theory, reading the history of later generations must trace its origins to ancient times in order to truly understand it. In fact, reading ancient history requires the history of later generations as a comparison in order to feel it is easy to understand." This is indeed the experience of studying history, and it is the path that beginners should take.

You can now be said to have a slight foundation in history (because you have already read many outlines of history and similar books). Therefore, our opinion on your future reading plan is that you do not need to study history for the time being but rather study methodology, because the difficulty you are currently feeling is that you feel these books cannot satisfy your desire for knowledge. However, these books are mostly not insufficient in material but rather incorrect in viewpoint. Therefore, you should first study methodology. After you have a rough understanding of this, you will have a central idea of your own. Then you can use this central idea to identify all theories and analyze and study all phenomena without wandering down the wrong path. ｜｜Kang

Letter to the Editor 189

To the Editor,

I am writing on behalf of my client, Mr. Sheng Yuliao, the former manager of the Sanxin Cotton Mill, who was shocked to read in today's newspaper about the Sanxin Cotton Mill workers' representatives declaring a hunger strike. The Tongshan Hall attached to the former Sanxin Cotton Mill was originally a charitable organization, and its annual expenses were often insufficient, relying on donations from the cotton mill for support. In the spring of 1931, when the Sanxin Cotton Mill was sold, I handed over all my duties and, according to the order of the Shanghai Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau, handed over all the assets of the Tongshan Hall, including more than 14 mu of land for burial, current funds of 1,923.90 yuan, and some materials. I immediately complied. Afterwards, I heard that the labor union organized by the workers in the factory had already submitted a report to the Social Affairs Bureau in April 1931, requesting a disposition. Therefore, the Social Affairs Bureau took this measure. Thus, my compliance with the order to hand over the assets was not only an administrative disposition by the Social Affairs Bureau but also the result of a petition by the workers' union. However, afterwards, some workers filed a criminal complaint against me for embezzlement in the First Special District Court. The court ruled that the case should be decided based on civil relations and transferred it to the Civil Division for trial. Later, the Civil Division held several hearings, and the workers requested an audit of the accounts. The court has appointed an accountant to audit the accounts, and both parties should wait for the court to resolve the matter. This is the true course of the case. The reports in the newspapers that there were large sums of money and a bail of 120,000 yuan in the Criminal Division are all fabricated and do not correspond to the facts. Yesterday morning, seven people claiming to be workers' representatives suddenly came to my residence. When they knocked on the door, they falsely claimed to be tailors and talked about the lawsuit. I replied peacefully and advised them to wait for the court's judgment. They still refused to leave. Later, the police intervened because they violated police regulations. I still believe that the workers were temporarily ignorant of the facts and did not harbor any resentment. However, today I saw in the newspaper that they exaggerated their claims and sensationalized the matter, and used inaccurate language to make veiled accusations, which is difficult to ignore. I have specially commissioned your esteemed lawyer to send a letter to various newspapers for correction, to set the record straight, and other matters. It is hoped that your esteemed newspaper will publish the original letter to clarify the matter. Thank you for your consideration. Sincerely, Lawyer Cai Liucheng, January 22.

Spring and Autumn

Boredom 190

— Yang Yusheng

Chinese people mostly like to talk about the weather when they meet, otherwise they can find a lot to say about "three meals a day"; this seems to have become a formula that can be applied everywhere.

Some people say this is "boring." Yes! Chinese people originally lived in "boredom", let alone now that we have encountered such a boring year!

The day before yesterday on Avenue Joffre, I inadvertently ran into a friend. The weather was very cloudy and humid that day, so after complaining about the weather, I asked him what he had been doing lately. He said a lot of the suffering he felt due to boredom.

I felt very regretful at the time. Because in this year of national chaos and people's livelihood is insecure, although there is no need to raise the whip of "national crisis" to force young people to embark on the path of struggle; but it is really unreasonable to force precious time under the name of "entertainment"! So I also felt a kind of boredom! We broke up in this boredom.

After I was squeezed onto the tram by many passengers like vicious criminals, regarding the question of why young people are so bored, perhaps because it is too serious, I couldn't investigate it for a while. At the same time, because my friend, although middle-aged, is still a "virgin", it reminded me of a "tragedy" many years ago.

There was a man and a woman who didn't know each other but studied in Beiping. I don't know why, but the man felt bored and the woman also felt bored; so, they often went to "Central Park" to run around without consulting each other. Soon, they gradually became closer, and they both felt they "had something". This can be said to be the end of everything. Because after another "soon", they still returned to "boredom" and finally sank into Kunming Lake and "died"!

The Classic of Mountains and Seas once said: "Ephemera fall to the ground and die after mating." According to this, the reason why "Ephemera" in the world are not extinct is that they must mate and think they have fulfilled their responsibilities before falling to the ground and dying. If Chinese people could become Ephemera, then not only could they be free from all boredom, but the world would be easier to save!

However, since it is called "man," the spirit of all things, his responsibility is certainly not as simple as that of an Ephemera. What is the responsibility of modern youth? Why do they feel bored? If the first question can be solved appropriately, the second question will not arise. Although they also feel the imperfection of social organization and the difficulty of the way out, and cannot avoid the attack of boredom; but this is still because the first question has not been "appropriately" solved.

If what they feel is a kind of "Ephemera-style" boredom, then it is not only the destruction of the youth itself, but also an irreparable loss to the country!

I always feel that Chinese people lack the spirit of "hard work" in various undertakings, and the call of "boredom" rushes out in the gaps of this spirit!

Watching Lanterns 191

— Hong Liao

The lanterns here are not the paper lanterns released on the fifteenth night of the lunar New Year, like rotating lanterns and rabbit lanterns. These lanterns shine every night of the 365 days of the year, indicating that they are decorations of the metropolis and a buffer zone in the tense atmosphere. But its role is exactly the same as paper rotating lanterns and rabbit lanterns. At the same time, taking advantage of the excitement, some novelties for people to enjoy have occupied a certain section in Shanghai and become a special area under its sphere of influence!

"What exactly is the novelty?"

"Where is the special area?"

Let me tell you - this special area is bordered by Zhejiang Road, Sixth Malu, Tibet Road, and Third Malu. Xiaohuayuan, Fuyu, Fuxiang, and Fuzhili are its main bases, and Qunyufang, Sanyuanfang, and Huilieli are its colonies. The atoms of the novelty are pink women. Chinese people have always called them "flowers." "Lanterns" are all kinds of things that use electricity to emit light. Merchants are used to using them as advertising tools. Smart "flowers" mark their own flower names on the "lanterns," relying on its colorfulness to attract some men to watch the lanterns. "The interpretation of watching lanterns is as such!"

"As long as you have money, it doesn't matter if they are strangers or acquaintances." These two sentences are a traditional policy of the "lantern flowers" to deal with the "lantern players." So the good lanterns are separated from the public and are only appreciated by those with big bellies and round faces! The remaining sour scholars often have to pass through this so-called special area. The "lantern" is still visible to you, but what about the "flower"? Except for occasionally smelling a nauseating smell naturally broadcast from it, don't have any other thoughts.

High Hats 192

— Mu Yin

In the past, there was a scholar who had just been appointed magistrate of a certain county. When he was about to take office, he went to his teacher's house to say goodbye as usual. His teacher said to him: "The gentry of a certain county are very cunning. You are an official for the first time. What do you rely on when you go there?"

"I just rely on my own knowledge." The scholar answered without hesitation.

"What's the use of knowledge?" His teacher shook his head repeatedly.

"I brought one hundred and twenty high hats." The scholar then told his teacher.

"What's the use of high hats?" His teacher still shook his head repeatedly.

"The teacher's prestige is known to everyone. I will tell them that I am the teacher's student, and they will naturally take care of me." The scholar changed his tone.

"That's okay..." His teacher immediately stopped shaking his head and smiled slightly.

"Teacher! I only have one hundred and nineteen high hats left now." The scholar told his teacher tightly.

"Why is there one less?" His teacher asked in a daze.

"That one was put on the teacher's head." The scholar also smiled slightly.

This kind of high hat has been loved by everyone since ancient times, and now it seems to be more fashionable. Some people, in order to decorate their own ugliness, do not hesitate to snatch this kind of hat from other people's heads and put it on their own heads. This clearly tells us that high hats have now become priceless treasures, and knowing how to give people high hats seems to be an essential skill in life now.

Authority of Marriage

Don't look down on this nonsense and eye-closing gentleman (because he is blind, he goes to fortune-telling, but fortune-tellers are not necessarily blind, but mostly use this as a guise to lure wealth and lust). He really holds the authority in life and marriage. No matter how like-minded and sympathetic you are, he can easily break up a pair of lovebirds with a few words. Fortunately, good men and women are obedient, and they always listen to him. Even if something unfortunate happens in the future, it is destined in the previous life and has nothing to do with others. He is an expert in bringing together estranged couples. If you want no estranged couples in the world, the initial task is to overthrow astrology.

Fourth Platoon Leader of Northeast China 194

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 23: The Pain is Unbearable, Concentrating on Listening to the Music, and the Joy is Not Satisfied, the Departure is Hasty, and the Flying Talisman Arrives

Not only Zhao's family was about to start being busy, but Yang's family also became busy. After Zhao Ziqiang returned home, he also met Guizhi twice. Because Guizhi was about to become a bride, if she talked to Ziqiang in front of people, she was afraid that the visiting relatives and friends would see it and make some jokes, so she only glanced at Ziqiang, indicating that I knew you were back, and still avoided it. Ziqiang originally thought about finding an opportunity to say a few words to Guizhi, but then he thought that he was about to get married. What can I talk about in the honeymoon, I can talk about what I am busy with now? So when he saw Guizhi, if there was someone, he looked at Guizhi and that's it. If there was no one, he smiled softly and said: You should be busy these few days. Is there anything I want you to prepare for me? Guizhi naturally smiled and said no. In addition, the two had no contact. But Guizhi's heart was carrying a question at this time. Like the relatives and friends in the family, busy coming and going, what did Gan Jiwu, who lived across the street, think? Because the mother was very suspicious of this matter, it was naturally inconvenient to ask. Apart from the mother, if she asked the second person, it would lead to suspicion even more, so although she couldn't help but feel puzzled, she just puzzled. But he was thinking right, Jizhi had not returned to Haitien, so he didn't have to worry too much about his situation. When he returned to Haitien, he happened to have met Guizhi and saw that a ray of her heart was still attached to him and had not changed. In addition, the second step, Guizhi suddenly disappeared, clearly putting him in a quiet place. If he wanted to avoid me, then when he saw me that time, he shouldn't have been so affectionate. When he was hesitating, he saw that the Zhao family's door was suddenly crowded with people coming in and out, and he was a little surprised, so he often walked outside the door and looked at the situation across the street.
